````
# Skill: openspec-explore

Enter explore mode. Think deeply. Visualize freely. Follow the conversation wherever it goes.

**IMPORTANT: Explore mode is for thinking, not implementing.** You may read files, search code, and investigate the codebase, but you must NEVER write code or implement features. If the user asks you to implement something, remind them to exit explore mode first (e.g., start a change with `/opsx:new` or `/opsx:ff`). You MAY create OpenSpec artifacts (proposals, designs, specs) if the user asks—that's capturing thinking, not implementing.

**This is a stance, not a workflow.** There are no fixed steps, no required sequence, no mandatory outputs. You're a thinking partner helping the user explore.

---

## The Stance

- **Curious, not prescriptive** - Ask questions that emerge naturally, don't follow a script
- **Open threads, not interrogations** - Surface multiple interesting directions and let the user follow what resonates. Don't funnel them through a single path of questions.
- **Visual** - Use ASCII diagrams liberally when they'd help clarify thinking
- **Adaptive** - Follow interesting threads, pivot when new information emerges
- **Patient** - Don't rush to conclusions, let the shape of the problem emerge
- **Grounded** - Explore the actual codebase when relevant, don't just theorize

---

## What You Might Do

Depending on what the user brings, you might:

**Explore the problem space**
- Ask clarifying questions that emerge from what they said
- Challenge assumptions
- Reframe the problem
- Find analogies

**Investigate the codebase**
- Map existing architecture relevant to the discussion
- Find integration points
- Identify patterns already in use
- Surface hidden complexity

**Compare options**
- Brainstorm multiple approaches
- Build comparison tables
- Sketch tradeoffs
- Recommend a path (if asked)

**Visualize**
```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐
│     Use ASCII diagrams liberally        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                         │
│   ┌────────┐         ┌────────┐        │
````

This is an interesting problem. It sounds like they're describing some kind of session management or workspace synchronization system. Let me think about what this could mean in different contexts:

1. **Git context**: They want to force pull from upstream, but that would overwrite local changes. They want to somehow "lock" the session after doing this.

2. **Real-time collaboration**: Like Google Docs or similar, where multiple people are editing, and someone wants to force sync to an authoritative version.

3. **State management**: In an application, there's an "upstream" state and a "local" state, and they want to force the local to match upstream but prevent further edits.

4. **VoIP/telecom context**: Given the project name seems to be "mimo" and there are VoIPStack references, this might be about call sessions or something related to the telephony system.

````
<type>file</type>
<content>1: # MIMO Platform
2: 
3: A minimal, Emacs-style web-based editor for AI-assisted development.
4: 
5: ## Overview
6: 
7: MIMO (Minimal IDE for Modern Operations) is a platform that enables AI-assisted development through a web-based interface with an Emacs-style workflow. It provides session-based development with worktrees, file synchronization, and integrated chat with AI agents.
8: 
9: ## Features
10: 
11: - **Public Landing Page**: View platform overview and public projects without authentication
12: - **Project Descriptions**: Add optional descriptions to projects for better discoverability
13: - **Emacs-Style Interface**: Three-buffer layout with customizable keybindings
14: - **Session-Based Development**: Work with isolated worktrees for each development session
15: - **File Synchronization**: Automatic sync between agent worktree and original repository
16: - **Integrated Chat**: Real-time chat with AI agents via WebSocket
17: - **VCS Integration**: Fossil as intermediary for both Git and Fossil repositories
18: - **Agent Lifecycle**: Spawn and manage AI agents with JWT authentication
19: - **Conflict Detection**: Smart conflict detection with baseline checksums
20: 
21: ## Architecture
22: 
23: ```
24: ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
25: │                      Browser (Client)                       │
26: │  ┌─────────────┐  ┌─────────────┐  ┌─────────────────┐   │
27: │  │ Files Tree  │  │   Chat      │  │    Changes      │   │
28: │  │   (Left)    │  │  (Center)   │  │    (Right)      │   │
29: │  └─────────────┘  └─────────────┘  └─────────────────┘   │
30: └─────────────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────┘
31:                           │ WebSocket / HTTP
32: ┌─────────────────────────▼─────────────────────────────────┐
33: │                 mimo-platform (Hono/Bun)                   │
34: │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
35: │  │  Auth  │  Projects  │  Sessions  │  Agents  │ Sync │  │
36: │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
37: │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
38: │  │              WebSocket Handlers                      │  │
39: │  │         (Chat, Agent Connections)                  │  │
40: │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
41: └─────────────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────┘
42:                           │
43: ┌─────────────────────────▼─────────────────────────────────┐
44: │                   mimo-agent (Binary)                      │
45: │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
46: │  │         File Watcher  │  ACP Process Proxy        │  │
47: │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
48: └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
49: ```
50: 
51: ## Installation
52: 
53: ### Prerequisites
54: 
55: - [Bun](https://bun.sh) 1.0+
56: - [Fossil](https://fossil-scm.org) 2.27+
57: - Git (for Git repository support)
58: 
59: ### Quick Start
60: 
61: ```bash
62: # Clone the repository
63: git clone https://github.com/your-org/mimo.git
64: cd mimo
65: 
66: # Install dependencies
67: cd packages/mimo-platform
68: bun install
69: 
70: # Start the server
71: bun run dev
72: ```
73: 
74: The platform will be available at `http://localhost:3000`
75: 
76: ### Build the Agent
77: 
78: ```bash
79: cd packages/mimo-agent
80: bun install
81: bun run build
82: ```
83: 
84: This creates `dist/mimo-agent` which is used by the platform.
85: 
86: ## Usage
87: 
88: ### Public Landing Page
89: 
90: When you first navigate to `http://localhost:3000`, you'll see a public landing page displaying:
91: - Platform overview and features
92: - List of all public projects (names, descriptions, owners, repo types)
93: - Login and Register buttons
94: 
95: Clicking on a project card will redirect you to login if not authenticated, or take you directly to the project detail if authenticated.
96: 
97: ### Authentication
98: 
99: 1. Navigate to `http://localhost:3000/auth/register`
100: 2. Create an account
101: 3. Login at `http://localhost:3000/auth/login`
102: 
103: ### Creating a Project
104: 
105: 1. Click "Create Project" on the projects page
106: 2. Enter project name
107: 3. Add an optional description (recommended ~200 chars, max 500)
108: 4. Provide Git or Fossil repository URL
109: 5. The system imports/clones the repository
110: 
111: ### Starting a Session
112: 
113: 1. Select a project from the projects list
114: 2. Click "New Session"
115: 3. Enter session name
116: 4. The system sets up a Fossil worktree
117: 
118: ### Working with Agents
119: 
120: 1. In a session, click "Start Agent"
121: 2. The platform spawns an agent process
122: 3. Chat with the agent in the center buffer
123: 4. File changes appear in the right buffer automatically
124: 
125: ### Committing Changes
126: 
127: 1. Make changes through the agent
128: 2. Click "Commit" button or press `C-x c`
129: 3. Enter commit message
130: 4. Changes are committed to Fossil and pushed to the original repository
131: 
132: ## Configuration
133: 
134: Configuration is stored in `~/.mimo/config.yaml`:
135: 
136: ```yaml
137: theme: dark
138: fontSize: 14
139: fontFamily: monospace
140: keybindings:
141:   cancel_request: "C-c C-c"
142:   commit: "C-x c"
143:   find_file: "C-x C-f"
144:   switch_project: "C-x p"
145:   switch_session: "C-x s"
146:   focus_left: "C-x h"
147:   focus_center: "C-x j"
148:   focus_right: "C-x l"
149: ```
150: 
151: Edit via the web UI at `/config` or directly in the file.
152: 
153: ## Directory Structure
154: 
155: ```
156: ~/.mimo/
157: ├── config.yaml           # User configuration
158: ├── users/
159: │   └── {username}/
160: │       └── credentials.yaml
161: ├── projects/
162: │   └── {project-id}/
163: │       ├── project.yaml
164: │       ├── repo.fossil
165: │       ├── original/     # Original repo worktree
166: │       └── sessions/
167: │           └── {session-id}/
168: │               ├── session.yaml
169: │               ├── chat.jsonl
170: │               ├── repo.fossil       # Fossil proxy for agent sync
171: │               ├── upstream/         # Original repository clone
172: │               └── agent-workspace/  # Agent working directory (plain files)
173: └── agents/
174:     └── {agent-id}/
175:         └── agent.yaml
176: ```
177: 
178: ### Session Directory Structure
179: 
180: Each session directory contains:
181: 
182: - `session.yaml` - Session metadata (name, status, port, agentWorkspacePath, upstreamPath)
183: - `chat.jsonl` - Chat message history
184: - `repo.fossil` - Fossil proxy repository for agent synchronization
185: - `upstream/` - Clone of the original repository (Git or Fossil)
186: - `agent-workspace/` - Working directory where agent makes edits (plain files, not a repository)
187: 
188: **Note:** The `agent-workspace/` was previously called `checkout/` but was renamed to clarify its purpose as a working directory rather than a repository checkout.
189: 
190: ## Commit and Push Flow
191: 
192: When you click "Commit" in a session, the system performs a 4-step commit flow:
193: 
194: 1. **Sync** (`fossil up`) - Synchronizes the agent-workspace with the latest changes from repo.fossil
195: 2. **Copy** (clean slate) - Copies all files from agent-workspace to upstream/ directory, removing old files
196: 3. **Commit** - Commits changes in the upstream/ directory with message "Mimo commit at <timestamp>"
197: 4. **Push** - Pushes the commit to the remote repository
198: 
199: The commit flow preserves VCS metadata (`.git/` or `.fossil`) during the copy operation.
200: 
201: ### Breaking Changes
202: 
203: **Old sessions need recreation**: Sessions created before the agent-workspace rename (v1.x) stored `checkoutPath` in session.yaml. These sessions will need to be recreated to work with the new commit flow.
204: 
205: ## Development
206: 
207: ```bash
208: # Run tests
209: bun test
210: 
211: # Run with hot reload
212: bun run dev
213: 
214: # Build for production
215: bun run build
216: ```
217:

219: 
220: MIT License - see LICENSE file for details.
221: 
222: ## Contributing
223: 
224: Contributions are welcome! Please read CONTRIBUTING.md for guidelines.
````

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 21:52:42)

Now I understand! This is the MIMO platform - a web-based editor with sessions and worktrees. The user is working on a **session** in this system.

Let me think about what they're asking...

The **session lifecycle** in MIMO:
- Sessions have `upstream/` - a clone of the original repository
- Sessions have `agent-workspace/` - where the agent makes edits
- The commit flow syncs from Fossil → agent-workspace → upstream

But the user wants a **force pull** - they made changes to the **external/upstream repository** and want to:
1. Pull those changes into their session
2. **Make the session read-only** afterward (no more interaction allowed)

This is essentially asking for a **"sync session with upstream then lock it"** feature.

The key insight is: **After force-pull, the session becomes read-only.** This is a safety mechanism - you can't accidentally overwrite upstream changes because you're locked out.

Let me visualize this:
## Agent (2026-04-08 21:52:47)

Now I see! This is MIMO - the web-based editor with sessions. You're working with **sessions** that have an `upstream/` directory containing a clone of the repository.

Let me trace through what you're describing:

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    SESSION LIFECYCLE                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

     External Repo                    Your Session
          │                              │
          │                              │
    ┌─────┴─────┐                  ┌─────┴─────┐
    │  ORIGIN   │                  │ UPSTREAM  │
    │  (live)   │◀─────────────────│  (clone)  │
    └─────┬─────┘                  └─────┬─────┘
          │                              │
          │                              ▼
          │                        ┌─────────────┐
          │                        │AGENT-WORKSP │

              push changes         └─────────────┘
```

You're saying: **"I made changes to ORIGIN externally, and I want to force my session to pull those changes and then become read-only."**

A few directions this could go:

**1. The "Rescue Sync" scenario**
You were working, stepped away, someone else pushed to origin, now your session is out of sync. You want to abandon your session's state and match origin, then lock it so you don't accidentally overwrite.

**2. The "Archive" scenario**  
This session is done, but you want one last sync with upstream before freezing it forever.

**3. The "Conflict Avoidance" scenario**
You know there are upstream changes that will conflict with your session. You want to see them without risking accidental commits.

Which resonates? Or is it something else entirely?

Also curious: **Why read-only?** Is this about preventing accidental edits, or is it more about signaling "this session is finished"?

The implementation could be as simple as a flag in `session.yaml`:
```yaml
status: readonly  # or locked, frozen, synced, etc.
```

But the *why* shapes the *what* here. What's driving this need?

## Agent (2026-04-08 22:11:44)

Ah, I see! I was conflating the session's `upstream/` with the project's state. Let me re-trace this...

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              MULTI-SESSION PROJECT ARCHITECTURE            │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

External Repo
     │
     │ (clone at project creation)
     ▼
┌────────────┐         Session A (created Monday)     Session B (created Wednesday)
│  PROJECT   │         ┌───────────────┐              ┌───────────────┐
│  original/ │         │ upstream/     │              │ upstream/     │
│  (latest)  │         │ (Monday's     │              │ (Wednesday's  │
└────────────┘         │  state)       │              │  state)       │
     ▲                 └───────────────┘              └───────────────┘
     │                         │                              │
     │                         ▼                              ▼
     │                  agent-workspace/                 agent-workspace/
     │                  (editing...)                     (editing...)
     │
     │ (external push happens Thursday)
     ▼
  STALE! ───────────────► Session A and B are now behind

```

So each session is essentially a **point-in-time snapshot** of the external repo. When the external repo moves forward, those sessions become stale. You want to:

1. **Detect staleness** - Compare session's upstream commit with external HEAD
2. **Mark as read-only** - Prevent edits on stale sessions
3. **Visual indicator** - Show in UI that session is outdated

**A few paths to explore:**

**Option A: Lazy Detection**
Check staleness when session is opened. If behind → mark readonly.

**Option B: Proactive Polling**
Background job checks all sessions periodically.

**Option C: Event-Driven**
Webhook/trigger when external repo changes (if you have push access to configure hooks).

**Option D: User-Initiated**
"Check for updates" button that user clicks, system compares and locks stale sessions.

Which feels right? Or is this triggered by something specific - like when the *project* itself pulls/fetches from external?

Also: When a session goes readonly, what should happen to the agent-workspace? Is it:
- Frozen (kept as-is for reference)?
- Cleared (can't do anything anyway)?
- Something else?

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 22:13:23)

The user wants Option E: an eager approach where when they force an update, the system searches for all sessions and makes them readonly. The agent-workspace should be frozen.

So the flow is:
1. User triggers "force update" (pull from external repo into the project)
2. System finds all sessions belonging to that project
3. Marks all those sessions as readonly
4. The agent-workspace is frozen (preserved but not editable)

This is about session lifecycle management when the upstream project changes.

Key questions to explore:
- How do sessions currently track their project affiliation?
- What's the current session status model?
- How would "force update" be triggered?
- What does "frozen" mean for agent-workspace? Just a flag, or actual filesystem permissions?

Let me think about the data model...

Project has:
- original/ directory (the repo)
- Multiple sessions

Session has:
- session.yaml with metadata
- upstream/ (point-in-time clone)
- agent-workspace/ (working directory)
- repo.fossil (sync proxy)

When project pulls from external:
- All sessions become stale
- Need to mark them readonly
- Preserve agent-workspace but freeze it

The "force pull" is an action that happens at the project level, not session level. It's saying "I want the project to match external, and I acknowledge this will invalidate existing sessions."

Session states could be:
- active (normal editing)
- readonly (frozen, viewing only)
- archived (completed, preserved for history)

Or maybe just a boolean `readonly: true` flag.

The eager approach makes sense here because:
- It prevents the "oops I edited a stale session" problem
- It's deterministic - happens immediately on force pull
- No polling or background jobs needed
- User intention is clear: "I'm taking over, everyone else watch only"

For the agent-workspace "frozen" state, I imagine:
- File watcher stops monitoring changes
- Agent can't write files
- UI shows read-only indicator
- But files remain accessible for viewing/reference

## Agent (2026-04-08 22:13:46)

Got it. **Option E: Eager invalidation on force update.**

When you force-pull the project, all sessions immediately become readonly. Clean, deterministic, no surprises.

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              EAGER SESSION INVALIDATION FLOW                 │

                         User Action
                            │

        │Session A│   │Session B│   │Session C│

        └────┬────┘   └────┬────┘   └────┬────┘
             │             │             │
             └─────────────┼─────────────┘
                           ▼

                   │  MARK ALL      │

                           │
              ┌────────────┼────────────┐

        ┌─────────┐   ┌─────────┐   ┌─────────┐
        │   🔒    │   │   🔒    │   │   🔒    │
        │ READONLY│   │ READONLY│   │ READONLY│
        │ agent-ws│   │ agent-ws│   │ agent-ws│

```

This creates a clear lifecycle:

```
══════════════

┌─────────┐    force pull     ┌─────────┐    resume?    ┌─────────┐
│ ACTIVE  │ ─────────────────▶ │READONLY │ ───────────▶ │ ACTIVE  │

└─────────┘                    └─────────┘              └─────────┘
      │                              │
      │ user closes                  │ user closes
      ▼                              ▼
┌─────────┐                    ┌─────────┐
│ARCHIVED │                    │ARCHIVED │
└─────────┘                    └─────────┘
```

   - Just a UI state (input disabled)?

```
<content>1: import { join } from "path";
2: import { existsSync, mkdirSync, writeFileSync, readFileSync, readdirSync, rmdirSync, unlinkSync } from "fs";
3: import { getPaths } from "../config/paths.js";
4: import { dump, load } from "js-yaml";
5: import crypto from "crypto";
6: 
7: export interface Session {
8:   id: string;
9:   name: string;
10:   projectId: string;
11:   owner: string;
12:   upstreamPath: string;

25: 
26: export interface SessionData {
27:   id: string;
28:   name: string;
29:   projectId: string;
30:   owner: string;
31:   upstreamPath: string;
32:   agentWorkspacePath: string;
33:   assignedAgentId?: string;
34:   status: "active" | "paused" | "closed";
35:   port: number | null;
36:   agentWorkspaceUser?: string;
37:   agentWorkspacePassword?: string;
38:   acpSessionId?: string;
39:   localDevMirrorPath?: string;
40:   agentSubpath?: string;
41:   createdAt: string;
42:   updatedAt: string;
43: }
44: 
45: export interface CreateSessionInput {
46:   name: string;
47:   projectId: string;
48:   owner: string;
49:   assignedAgentId?: string;
50:   localDevMirrorPath?: string;
51:   agentSubpath?: string;
52: }
53: 
54: export class SessionRepository {
55:   private getSessionPath(projectId: string, sessionId: string): string {
56:     return join(getPaths().projects, projectId, "sessions", sessionId);
57:   }
58: 
59:   private getSessionFilePath(projectId: string, sessionId: string): string {
60:     return join(this.getSessionPath(projectId, sessionId), "session.yaml");
61:   }
62: 
63:   private getUpstreamPath(projectId: string, sessionId: string): string {
64:     return join(this.getSessionPath(projectId, sessionId), "upstream");
65:   }
66: 
67:   private getAgentWorkspacePath(projectId: string, sessionId: string): string {
68:     return join(this.getSessionPath(projectId, sessionId), "agent-workspace");
69:   }
70: 
71:   private generateId(): string {
72:     return crypto.randomUUID();
73:   }
74: 
75:   async create(input: CreateSessionInput): Promise<Session> {
76:     const id = this.generateId();
77:     const sessionPath = this.getSessionPath(input.projectId, id);
78:     const upstreamPath = this.getUpstreamPath(input.projectId, id);
79:     const agentWorkspacePath = this.getAgentWorkspacePath(input.projectId, id);
80: 
81:     // Create session directory
82:     if (!existsSync(sessionPath)) {
83:       mkdirSync(sessionPath, { recursive: true });
84:     }
85: 
86:     // Create upstream directory
87:     if (!existsSync(upstreamPath)) {
88:       mkdirSync(upstreamPath, { recursive: true });
89:     }
90: 
91:     // Create agent-workspace directory
92:     if (!existsSync(agentWorkspacePath)) {
93:       mkdirSync(agentWorkspacePath, { recursive: true });
94:     }
95: 
96:     const now = new Date().toISOString();
97:     const sessionData: SessionData = {
98:       id,
99:       name: input.name,
100:       projectId: input.projectId,
101:       owner: input.owner,
102:       upstreamPath,
103:       agentWorkspacePath,
104:       assignedAgentId: input.assignedAgentId,
105:       status: "active",
106:       port: null,
107:       createdAt: now,
108:       updatedAt: now,
109:       ...(input.localDevMirrorPath && { localDevMirrorPath: input.localDevMirrorPath }),
110:       ...(input.agentSubpath && { agentSubpath: input.agentSubpath }),
111:     };
112: 
113:     writeFileSync(
114:       this.getSessionFilePath(input.projectId, id),
115:       dump(sessionData),
116:       "utf-8"
117:     );
118: 
119:     return {
120:       ...sessionData,
121:       createdAt: new Date(sessionData.createdAt),
122:       updatedAt: new Date(sessionData.updatedAt),
123:     };
124:   }
125: 
126:   async findById(sessionId: string): Promise<Session | null> {
127:     // Search across all projects for the session
128:     const Paths = getPaths();
129:     if (!existsSync(Paths.projects)) {
130:       return null;
131:     }
132: 
133:     const projectEntries = readdirSync(Paths.projects, { withFileTypes: true });
134:     
135:     for (const projectEntry of projectEntries) {
136:       if (projectEntry.isDirectory()) {
137:         const sessionsDir = join(Paths.projects, projectEntry.name, "sessions");
138:         if (existsSync(sessionsDir)) {
139:           const sessionFile = join(sessionsDir, sessionId, "session.yaml");
140:           if (existsSync(sessionFile)) {
141:             const content = readFileSync(sessionFile, "utf-8");
142:             const data = load(content) as SessionData;
143:             // Handle migration from checkoutPath to agentWorkspacePath
144:             const sessionData = {
145:               ...data,
146:               agentWorkspacePath: data.agentWorkspacePath || (data as any).checkoutPath,
147:             };
148:             return {
149:               ...sessionData,
150:               createdAt: new Date(data.createdAt),
151:               updatedAt: new Date(data.updatedAt),
152:             };
153:           }
154:         }
155:       }
156:     }
157: 
158:     return null;
159:   }
160:

184:     if (!existsSync(sessionsDir)) {
185:       return [];
186:     }

201:           };
202:           sessions.push({
203:             ...sessionData,
204:             createdAt: new Date(data.createdAt),
205:             updatedAt: new Date(data.updatedAt),
206:           });
207:         }
208:       }
209:     }
210: 
211:     return sessions.sort((a, b) => b.createdAt.getTime() - a.createdAt.getTime());
212:   }
213: 
214:   async findByAssignedAgentId(agentId: string): Promise<Session[]> {
215:     const Paths = getPaths();
216:     if (!existsSync(Paths.projects)) {
217:       return [];
218:     }
219: 
220:     const projectEntries = readdirSync(Paths.projects, { withFileTypes: true });
221:     const sessions: Session[] = [];
222: 
223:     for (const projectEntry of projectEntries) {
224:       if (projectEntry.isDirectory()) {
225:         const sessionsDir = join(Paths.projects, projectEntry.name, "sessions");
226:         if (existsSync(sessionsDir)) {
227:           const entries = readdirSync(sessionsDir, { withFileTypes: true });
228:           for (const entry of entries) {
229:             if (entry.isDirectory()) {
230:               const sessionFile = join(sessionsDir, entry.name, "session.yaml");
231:               if (existsSync(sessionFile)) {
232:                 const content = readFileSync(sessionFile, "utf-8");
233:                 const data = load(content) as SessionData;
234:                 // Handle migration from checkoutPath to agentWorkspacePath
235:                 const sessionData = {
236:                   ...data,
237:                   agentWorkspacePath: data.agentWorkspacePath || (data as any).checkoutPath,
238:                 };
239:                 if (data.assignedAgentId === agentId) {
240:                   sessions.push({
241:                     ...sessionData,
242:                     createdAt: new Date(data.createdAt),
243:                     updatedAt: new Date(data.updatedAt),
244:                   });
245:                 }
246:               }
247:             }
248:           }
249:         }
250:       }
251:     }

254:   }

256:   async update(sessionId: string, updates: Partial<Omit<SessionData, "id" | "createdAt">>): Promise<Session | null> {
257:     const session = await this.findById(sessionId);
258:     if (!session) return null;
259: 
260:     const updatedData: SessionData = {
261:       ...session,
262:       ...updates,
263:       updatedAt: new Date().toISOString(),
264:     };
265: 
266:     const filePath = this.getSessionFilePath(session.projectId, sessionId);
267:     writeFileSync(filePath, dump(updatedData), "utf-8");
268: 
269:     return {
270:       ...updatedData,
271:       createdAt: new Date(updatedData.createdAt),
272:       updatedAt: new Date(updatedData.updatedAt),
273:     };
274:   }
275: 
276:   async delete(projectId: string, sessionId: string): Promise<void> {
277:     const sessionPath = this.getSessionPath(projectId, sessionId);
278:     
279:     // Delete entire session directory (includes upstream/, agent-workspace/, repo.fossil, session.yaml)
280:     if (existsSync(sessionPath)) {
281:       this.deleteDirectoryRecursive(sessionPath);
282:     }
283:   }
284: 
285:   private deleteDirectoryRecursive(dirPath: string): void {
286:     if (!existsSync(dirPath)) return;
287: 
288:     const entries = readdirSync(dirPath, { withFileTypes: true });
289:     
290:     for (const entry of entries) {
291:       const entryPath = join(dirPath, entry.name);
292:       if (entry.isDirectory()) {
293:         this.deleteDirectoryRecursive(entryPath);
294:       } else {
295:         unlinkSync(entryPath);
296:       }
297:     }
298: 
299:     rmdirSync(dirPath);
300:   }
301: 
302:   async exists(projectId: string, sessionId: string): Promise<boolean> {
303:     return existsSync(this.getSessionFilePath(projectId, sessionId));
304:   }
305: }
```

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 22:14:51)

Okay, now I have a good picture. Let me summarize what I've learned:

**Current Session Status Flow:**
- Sessions have status: `"active" | "paused" | "closed"`
- Sessions belong to projects via `projectId`
- Each session has its own `upstream/` directory (a clone at creation time)
- Each session has an `agent-workspace/` directory where the agent edits

**What user wants (Option E - Eager Invalidation):**
1. User triggers "force pull" on a project
2. System updates the project's `original/` directory with external changes
3. System finds ALL sessions for that project
4. System marks ALL those sessions as `readonly`
5. System "freezes" the agent-workspace (no more edits)

**Key Design Decisions to Explore:**

1. **Session Status**: Add `"readonly"` as a new status, or is this something else?
   - Could be a separate flag `isStale: true` 
   - Or a new status `"stale"` or `"readonly"`

2. **"Force Pull" Location**: 
   - New route: `POST /projects/:id/force-pull`
   - Or part of existing sync service?

3. **Freezing agent-workspace**:
   - Just a status check in the file watcher?
   - File system level (chmod)?
   - Both?

4. **UX Considerations**:
   - What message does user see when trying to edit a readonly session?
   - Can they "unfreeze" by pulling updates to their session's upstream?
   - Or is the only path: archive → create new session?

This is enough thinking to start formalizing. The user seems to have a clear vision - eager invalidation, freeze all sessions, agent-workspace locked. Should offer to capture this as an OpenSpec change.
## Agent (2026-04-08 22:14:58)

Now I have the full picture. Let me visualize the eager invalidation approach:

```
PROJECT FORCE PULL WITH SESSION INVALIDATION
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

User Action: "Force Pull & Replace"
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  POST /projects/:id/force-pull                          │
│  Body: { strategy: "replace", invalidateSessions: true } │
└─────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┘
                          │
                          ▼
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  1. Fetch external changes to project/original/         │
│  2. For each session in project:                        │
│       ┌─────────────┐                                   │
│       │ Session A   │ ──▶ status: "readonly"            │
│       │ Session B   │ ──▶ status: "readonly"            │
│       │ Session C   │ ──▶ status: "readonly"            │
│       └─────────────┘                                   │
│  3. Mark agent-workspaces frozen (no file writes)       │
└─────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┘
                          │
                          ▼
           Sessions are now VIEW-ONLY
           Can browse chat history, see files
           Cannot edit, cannot commit
```

**Key insight**: The session's `upstream/` doesn't get updated - it's intentionally left as a **snapshot of the stale state**. This preserves the historical context. The agent-workspace is frozen, not deleted.

**Recovery paths for a readonly session:**

```
SESSION LIFECYCLE AFTER FORCE PULL
═══════════════════════════════════════════

     ┌─────────────┐
     │   ACTIVE    │
     │  (editing)  │
     └──────┬──────┘
            │
            ▼ Force Pull on Project
     ┌─────────────┐
     │  READONLY   │◄──────────────────────┐
     │  (frozen)   │                       │
     └──────┬──────┘                       │
            │                              │
    ┌───────┴───────┐                      │
    │               │                      │
    ▼               ▼                      │
┌─────────┐    ┌─────────┐                │
│ Archive │    │ Resume? │ ──▶ No         │
│  (done) │    │         │ ──▶ Yes        │
└─────────┘    └────┬────┘                │
                    │                      │
                    ▼                      │
            ┌─────────────┐                │
            │ Create NEW  │                │
            │  session    │                │
            │ (fresh clone)               │
            └─────────────┘                │
                                           │
            Old session stays              │
            READONLY forever ──────────────┘
```

**Open questions for you:**

1. **Status naming**: `"readonly"` or `"stale"` or `"frozen"`? I lean toward `"stale"` because it explains *why*.

2. **Freezing mechanism**: Should the file watcher just check status and refuse writes? Or also `chmod -R -w` on agent-workspace for extra safety?

3. **UI indicator**: Just a badge on the session? Or a full banner explaining "This session is stale - external changes detected"?

4. **What happens to running agents?** If Session A has an active agent process when force pull happens, should it be:
   - Killed immediately?
   - Allowed to finish current operation then shut down?
   - Just forbidden from making new file changes?

5. **Should force-pull be undoable?** Like a "restore previous state" option?

This feels like a solid, clean feature. Want me to capture this as an OpenSpec change so you can start implementing? Or keep exploring edge cases?

2. not need any change in agent-workspace
3. good idea a badge
4. not need any action
5. not, not revert

Also i want the action not inside edit the project, i want at the button closer to Delete Project

The user has clarified their requirements:

**What "frozen" prevents:**

**Summary of what we landed on:**

| Aspect | Decision |
|--------|----------|
| **Status name** | `frozen` (new enum value) |
| **Trigger** | POST `/projects/:id/freeze` button |
| **Effect** | All sessions for project → `status: "frozen"` |
| **Badge** | 🔒 FROZEN on both project header and sessions |

| **Agent-workspace** | No changes - just don't allow edits |
| **Running agents** | No action - continue as-is |
| **Revert** | Not supported |

**What's frozen prevents:**
- File edits (file watcher checks `session.status !== 'frozen'`)
- Commits (commit button disabled or backend rejects)
- Possibly: starting new agents

**What's frozen allows:**
- Browse files read-only
- View chat history
- Running agents continue working

```
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

The simplicity is:
1. Freeze project → all sessions get `status: "frozen"`
2. In session UI, chat input is disabled if status === "frozen"
3. Sessions list shows "frozen" status
4. Nothing else changes - agent-workspace untouched, running agents can finish, file watcher unaffected

The key insight: **frozen is about communication, not files**. No edits because no agent to make them. No commits because no new changes to commit.

### Tool Call [completed]: Loaded skill: openspec-ff-change

**Tool:** other
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:20:26
**Parameters:**
name: openspec-ff-change

````
<skill_content name="openspec-ff-change">
# Skill: openspec-ff-change

Fast-forward through artifact creation - generate everything needed to start implementation in one go.

**Input**: The user's request should include a change name (kebab-case) OR a description of what they want to build.

**Steps**

1. **If no clear input provided, ask what they want to build**

   Use the **AskUserQuestion tool** (open-ended, no preset options) to ask:
   > "What change do you want to work on? Describe what you want to build or fix."

   From their description, derive a kebab-case name (e.g., "add user authentication" → `add-user-auth`).

   **IMPORTANT**: Do NOT proceed without understanding what the user wants to build.

2. **Create the change directory**
   ```bash
   openspec new change "<name>"
   ```
   This creates a scaffolded change at `openspec/changes/<name>/`.

3. **Get the artifact build order**
   ```bash
   openspec status --change "<name>" --json
   ```
   Parse the JSON to get:
   - `applyRequires`: array of artifact IDs needed before implementation (e.g., `["tasks"]`)
   - `artifacts`: list of all artifacts with their status and dependencies

4. **Create artifacts in sequence until apply-ready**

   Use the **TodoWrite tool** to track progress through the artifacts.

   Loop through artifacts in dependency order (artifacts with no pending dependencies first):

   a. **For each artifact that is `ready` (dependencies satisfied)**:
      - Get instructions:
        ```bash
        openspec instructions <artifact-id> --change "<name>" --json
        ```
      - The instructions JSON includes:
        - `context`: Project background (constraints for you - do NOT include in output)
        - `rules`: Artifact-specific rules (constraints for you - do NOT include in output)
        - `template`: The structure to use for your output file
        - `instruction`: Schema-specific guidance for this artifact type
        - `outputPath`: Where to write the artifact
        - `dependencies`: Completed artifacts to read for context
      - Read any completed dependency files for context
      - Create the artifact file using `template` as the structure
      - Apply `context` and `rules` as constraints - but do NOT copy them into the file
      - Show brief progress: "✓ Created <artifact-id>"

   b. **Continue until all `applyRequires` artifacts are complete**
      - After creating each artifact, re-run `openspec status --change "<name>" --json`
      - Check if every artifact ID in `applyRequires` has `status: "done"` in the artifacts array
      - Stop when all `applyRequires` artifacts are done

   c. **If an artifact requires user input** (unclear context):
      - Use **AskUserQuestion tool** to clarify
      - Then continue with creation

5. **Show final status**
   ```bash
   openspec status --change "<name>"
   ```

**Output**

After completing all artifacts, summarize:
- Change name and location
- List of artifacts created with brief descriptions
- What's ready: "All artifacts created! Ready for implementation."
- Prompt: "Run `/opsx:apply` or ask me to implement to start working on the tasks."

**Artifact Creation Guidelines**

- Follow the `instruction` field from `openspec instructions` for each artifact type
- The schema defines what each artifact should contain - follow it
- Read dependency artifacts for context before creating new ones
- Use `template` as the structure for your output file - fill in its sections
- **IMPORTANT**: `context` and `rules` are constraints for YOU, not content for the file
  - Do NOT copy `<context>`, `<rules>`, `<project_context>` blocks into the artifact
  - These guide what you write, but should never appear in the output

**Guardrails**
- Create ALL artifacts needed for implementation (as defined by schema's `apply.requires`)
- Always read dependency artifacts before creating a new one
- If context is critically unclear, ask the user - but prefer making reasonable decisions to keep momentum
- If a change with that name already exists, suggest continuing that change instead
- Verify each artifact file exists after writing before proceeding to next
````

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/project-freeze/proposal.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:21:20
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/project-freeze/proposal.md
content: ## Why

When external changes are pushed to a project's upstream repository, existing sessions become stale. Users need a way to mark all sessions as frozen to prevent accidental edits on outdated state. Currently, there's no mechanism to lock sessions when the external repository has moved forward.

## What Changes

- Add `frozen` status to session status enum (`active | paused | closed` → `active | paused | closed | frozen`)
- Create new project action "Freeze Project" that marks all sessions as `frozen`
- Add "Freeze Project" button to Project Detail page (Actions section, next to Delete)
- Block chat message sending for frozen sessions
- Block commit operations for frozen sessions
- Display `frozen` status in sessions list (no badge/icon, just text)

## Capabilities

### New Capabilities
- `session-freeze`: Session status management with frozen state and project-level freeze action

### Modified Capabilities
- None (existing session behavior remains unchanged, just adding new status value)

## Impact

- Session repository: new `frozen` status value
- Project Detail UI: new button and action
- Session routes: validation to block messages/commits for frozen sessions
- Session list UI: display frozen status


```

+
+## What Changes
+
+- Add `frozen` status to session status enum (`active | paused | closed` → `active | paused | closed | frozen`)
+- Create new project action "Freeze Project" that marks all sessions as `frozen`
+- Add "Freeze Project" button to Project Detail page (Actions section, next to Delete)
+- Block chat message sending for frozen sessions
+- Block commit operations for frozen sessions
+- Display `frozen` status in sessions list (no badge/icon, just text)
+
+## Capabilities
+
+### New Capabilities
+- `session-freeze`: Session status management with frozen state and project-level freeze action
+
+### Modified Capabilities
+- None (existing session behavior remains unchanged, just adding new status value)
+
+## Impact
+
+- Session repository: new `frozen` status value
+- Project Detail UI: new button and action
+- Session routes: validation to block messages/commits for frozen sessions
```

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 22:21:44)

Now I have the proposal context. Let me create the design document.

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/project-freeze/design.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:22:00
**Parameters:**
content: ## Context

The MIMO platform uses sessions to isolate work on projects. Each session has a `status` field currently supporting `active`, `paused`, and `closed`. When external changes occur in the upstream repository, users need a way to freeze all sessions to prevent editing stale state.

The freeze operation is a project-level action that affects all sessions belonging to that project. Once frozen, sessions remain viewable but cannot accept new edits or commits.

## Goals / Non-Goals

**Goals:**
- Provide a one-click "Freeze Project" action that marks all sessions as `frozen`
- Prevent chat message sending on frozen sessions
- Prevent commit operations on frozen sessions
- Display `frozen` status clearly in the sessions list

**Non-Goals:**
- Automatic freeze detection (this is manual user action)
- Unfreezing sessions (create new sessions instead)
- Visual badges or icons (just status text)
- Changes to agent-workspace file system
- Interruption of running agents

## Decisions

**1. New `frozen` status value**
- Extends existing status enum: `"active" | "paused" | "closed" | "frozen"`
- Frozen sessions are distinct from paused (paused can be resumed, frozen cannot)
- Simple enum addition avoids complex state machines

**2. Project-level freeze action**
- POST endpoint: `/projects/:id/freeze`
- Iterates all sessions for the project and updates status to `frozen`
- No atomic transaction needed (eventual consistency is acceptable)

**3. Minimal UI changes**
- Single "Freeze Project" button in Project Detail Actions section
- Status displays as plain text "frozen" in sessions list
- No special styling or badges requested

**4. Blocking at API level**
- Check `session.status === 'frozen'` before processing chat messages
- Check `session.status === 'frozen'` before processing commits
- Return appropriate error message indicating session is frozen

## Risks / Trade-offs

- **Risk**: Users may accidentally freeze projects
  - Mitigation: Add confirmation dialog (optional, can be skipped per user preference)
  
- **Risk**: Frozen sessions accumulate over time
  - Mitigation: Archive functionality already exists for cleanup

- **Trade-off**: No unfreeze operation means users must create new sessions
  - Rationale: Keeps implementation simple, frozen sessions serve as historical record

filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/project-freeze/design.md

```

@@ -0,0 +1,53 @@
+## Context
+
+The MIMO platform uses sessions to isolate work on projects. Each session has a `status` field currently supporting `active`, `paused`, and `closed`. When external changes occur in the upstream repository, users need a way to freeze all sessions to prevent editing stale state.
+
+The freeze operation is a project-level action that affects all sessions belonging to that project. Once frozen, sessions remain viewable but cannot accept new edits or commits.
+
+## Goals / Non-Goals
+
+**Goals:**
+- Provide a one-click "Freeze Project" action that marks all sessions as `frozen`
+- Prevent chat message sending on frozen sessions
+- Prevent commit operations on frozen sessions
+- Display `frozen` status clearly in the sessions list
+
+**Non-Goals:**
+- Automatic freeze detection (this is manual user action)
+- Unfreezing sessions (create new sessions instead)
+- Visual badges or icons (just status text)
+- Changes to agent-workspace file system
+- Interruption of running agents
+
+## Decisions
+
+**1. New `frozen` status value**
+- Extends existing status enum: `"active" | "paused" | "closed" | "frozen"`
+- Frozen sessions are distinct from paused (paused can be resumed, frozen cannot)
+- Simple enum addition avoids complex state machines
+
+**2. Project-level freeze action**
+- POST endpoint: `/projects/:id/freeze`
+- Iterates all sessions for the project and updates status to `frozen`
+- No atomic transaction needed (eventual consistency is acceptable)
+
+**3. Minimal UI changes**
+- Single "Freeze Project" button in Project Detail Actions section
+- Status displays as plain text "frozen" in sessions list
+- No special styling or badges requested
+
+**4. Blocking at API level**
+- Check `session.status === 'frozen'` before processing chat messages
+- Check `session.status === 'frozen'` before processing commits
+- Return appropriate error message indicating session is frozen
+
+## Risks / Trade-offs
+
+- **Risk**: Users may accidentally freeze projects
+  - Mitigation: Add confirmation dialog (optional, can be skipped per user preference)
+  
+- **Risk**: Frozen sessions accumulate over time
+  - Mitigation: Archive functionality already exists for cleanup
+
+- **Trade-off**: No unfreeze operation means users must create new sessions
+  - Rationale: Keeps implementation simple, frozen sessions serve as historical record
```

````
- Generating instructions...
{
  "changeName": "project-freeze",
  "artifactId": "specs",
  "schemaName": "spec-driven",
  "changeDir": "/home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/project-freeze",
  "outputPath": "specs/**/*.md",
  "description": "Detailed specifications for the change",
  "instruction": "Create specification files that define WHAT the system should do.\n\nCreate one spec file per capability listed in the proposal's Capabilities section.\n- New capabilities: use the exact kebab-case name from the proposal (specs/<capability>/spec.md).\n- Modified capabilities: use the existing spec folder name from openspec/specs/<capability>/ when creating the delta spec at specs/<capability>/spec.md.\n\nDelta operations (use ## headers):\n- **ADDED Requirements**: New capabilities\n- **MODIFIED Requirements**: Changed behavior - MUST include full updated content\n- **REMOVED Requirements**: Deprecated features - MUST include **Reason** and **Migration**\n- **RENAMED Requirements**: Name changes only - use FROM:/TO: format\n\nFormat requirements:\n- Each requirement: `### Requirement: <name>` followed by description\n- Use SHALL/MUST for normative requirements (avoid should/may)\n- Each scenario: `#### Scenario: <name>` with WHEN/THEN format\n- **CRITICAL**: Scenarios MUST use exactly 4 hashtags (`####`). Using 3 hashtags or bullets will fail silently.\n- Every requirement MUST have at least one scenario.\n\nMODIFIED requirements workflow:\n1. Locate the existing requirement in openspec/specs/<capability>/spec.md\n2. Copy the ENTIRE requirement block (from `### Requirement:` through all scenarios)\n3. Paste under `## MODIFIED Requirements` and edit to reflect new behavior\n4. Ensure header text matches exactly (whitespace-insensitive)\n\nCommon pitfall: Using MODIFIED with partial content loses detail at archive time.\nIf adding new concerns without changing existing behavior, use ADDED instead.\n\nExample:\n```\n## ADDED Requirements\n\n### Requirement: User can export data\nThe system SHALL allow users to export their data in CSV format.\n\n#### Scenario: Successful export\n- **WHEN** user clicks \"Export\" button\n- **THEN** system downloads a CSV file with all user data\n\n## REMOVED Requirements\n\n### Requirement: Legacy export\n**Reason**: Replaced by new export system\n**Migration**: Use new export endpoint at /api/v2/export\n```\n\nSpecs should be testable - each scenario is a potential test case.\n",
  "template": "## ADDED Requirements\n\n### Requirement: <!-- requirement name -->\n<!-- requirement text -->\n\n#### Scenario: <!-- scenario name -->\n- **WHEN** <!-- condition -->\n- **THEN** <!-- expected outcome -->\n",
  "dependencies": [
    {
      "id": "proposal",
      "done": true,
      "path": "proposal.md",
      "description": "Initial proposal document outlining the change"
    }
  ],
  "unlocks": [
````

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 22:22:17)

**Spec for Session Freeze**

Now I need to create the spec for `session-freeze` capability with detailed requirements and scenarios.

Requirements:
1. Session status enum includes `frozen`
2. Project freeze endpoint exists and works
3. Chat messages blocked for frozen sessions
4. Commits blocked for frozen sessions
5. Frozen status displayed in sessions list

Let me write this spec.

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/project-freeze/specs/session-freeze/spec.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:22:40
**Parameters:**
content: ## ADDED Requirements

### Requirement: Session status includes frozen state
The session status enum SHALL include `frozen` as a valid status value.

#### Scenario: Session created with active status
- **WHEN** a new session is created
- **THEN** the session status SHALL be set to `active`

#### Scenario: Session status can be set to frozen
- **GIVEN** a session with status `active`
- **WHEN** the session status is updated to `frozen`
- **THEN** the session status SHALL be `frozen`

### Requirement: Project freeze action marks all sessions as frozen
The system SHALL provide a project-level action that marks all sessions belonging to that project as `frozen`.

#### Scenario: Freeze project with multiple sessions
- **GIVEN** a project with 3 sessions (all with status `active`)
- **WHEN** the "Freeze Project" action is invoked
- **THEN** all 3 sessions SHALL have status `frozen`

#### Scenario: Freeze project with no sessions
- **GIVEN** a project with 0 sessions
- **WHEN** the "Freeze Project" action is invoked
- **THEN** no error SHALL occur

#### Scenario: Freeze project with mixed session statuses
- **GIVEN** a project with sessions having statuses `active`, `paused`, and `closed`
- **WHEN** the "Freeze Project" action is invoked
- **THEN** all sessions SHALL have status `frozen`

### Requirement: Chat messages blocked for frozen sessions
The system SHALL reject chat message requests for sessions with status `frozen`.

#### Scenario: Send message to frozen session
- **GIVEN** a session with status `frozen`
- **WHEN** a chat message is sent to that session
- **THEN** the system SHALL return an error indicating the session is frozen
- **AND** the message SHALL NOT be processed

#### Scenario: Send message to active session
- **GIVEN** a session with status `active`
- **WHEN** a chat message is sent to that session
- **THEN** the message SHALL be processed normally

### Requirement: Commits blocked for frozen sessions
The system SHALL reject commit requests for sessions with status `frozen`.

#### Scenario: Commit from frozen session
- **GIVEN** a session with status `frozen`
- **WHEN** a commit is attempted from that session
- **THEN** the system SHALL return an error indicating the session is frozen
- **AND** the commit SHALL NOT be executed

#### Scenario: Commit from active session
- **GIVEN** a session with status `active`
- **WHEN** a commit is attempted from that session
- **THEN** the commit SHALL be executed normally

### Requirement: Frozen status displayed in sessions list
The system SHALL display the `frozen` status in the sessions list.

#### Scenario: View sessions list with frozen session
- **GIVEN** a project with one session having status `frozen`
- **WHEN** the sessions list is viewed
- **THEN** the session SHALL display status as "frozen"

### Requirement: Freeze project button in UI
The system SHALL provide a "Freeze Project" button on the Project Detail page.

#### Scenario: Project detail page displays freeze button
- **GIVEN** a project exists
- **WHEN** the Project Detail page is viewed
- **THEN** a "Freeze Project" button SHALL be visible in the Actions section

#### Scenario: Click freeze button
- **GIVEN** the Project Detail page is displayed
- **WHEN** the "Freeze Project" button is clicked
- **THEN** all sessions for the project SHALL be marked as `frozen`
- **AND** the page SHALL reflect the updated statuses

filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/project-freeze/specs/session-freeze/spec.md


- [ ] 3.2 Return error response when session is frozen

- [ ] 4.2 Return error response when session is frozen

- [ ] 5.2 Create POST form for freeze action
- [ ] 5.3 Verify `frozen` status displays correctly in sessions list

- [ ] 6.2 Test freeze action marks all project sessions as frozen
- [ ] 6.3 Test chat messages blocked for frozen sessions
- [ ] 6.4 Test commits blocked for frozen sessions

| Artifact | Description |

| **design.md** | Technical approach: new `frozen` status, POST `/projects/:id/freeze`, API-level blocking |
| **specs/session-freeze/spec.md** | 6 requirements with scenarios: status enum, freeze action, chat blocking, commit blocking, UI display, button |
| **tasks.md** | 6 task groups: status type, freeze action, chat blocking, commit blocking, UI updates, tests |

- POST `/projects/:id/freeze` marks all sessions as frozen
- Block chat messages and commits for frozen sessions

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 22:23:54)

The user wants me to implement the tasks from the `project-freeze` change. Let me follow the steps:

1. Select the change: The user provided "project-freeze"
2. Check status
3. Get apply instructions
4. Read context files
5. Show progress
6. Implement tasks
7. Show status

Let me start by checking the status and getting the apply instructions.

### Tool Call [completed]: Loaded skill: openspec-apply-change

**Tool:** other
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:23:56
**Parameters:**
name: openspec-apply-change

````
<skill_content name="openspec-apply-change">
# Skill: openspec-apply-change

Implement tasks from an OpenSpec change.

**Input**: Optionally specify a change name. If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.

**Steps**

1. **Select the change**

   If a name is provided, use it. Otherwise:
   - Infer from conversation context if the user mentioned a change
   - Auto-select if only one active change exists
   - If ambiguous, run `openspec list --json` to get available changes and use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select

   Always announce: "Using change: <name>" and how to override (e.g., `/opsx:apply <other>`).

2. **Check status to understand the schema**
   ```bash
   openspec status --change "<name>" --json
   ```
   Parse the JSON to understand:
   - `schemaName`: The workflow being used (e.g., "spec-driven")
   - Which artifact contains the tasks (typically "tasks" for spec-driven, check status for others)

3. **Get apply instructions**

   ```bash
   openspec instructions apply --change "<name>" --json
   ```

   This returns:
   - Context file paths (varies by schema - could be proposal/specs/design/tasks or spec/tests/implementation/docs)
   - Progress (total, complete, remaining)
   - Task list with status
   - Dynamic instruction based on current state

   **Handle states:**
   - If `state: "blocked"` (missing artifacts): show message, suggest using openspec-continue-change
   - If `state: "all_done"`: congratulate, suggest archive
   - Otherwise: proceed to implementation

4. **Read context files**

   Read the files listed in `contextFiles` from the apply instructions output.
   The files depend on the schema being used:
   - **spec-driven**: proposal, specs, design, tasks
   - Other schemas: follow the contextFiles from CLI output

5. **Show current progress**

   Display:
   - Schema being used
   - Progress: "N/M tasks complete"
   - Remaining tasks overview
   - Dynamic instruction from CLI

6. **Implement tasks (loop until done or blocked)**

   For each pending task:
   - Show which task is being worked on
   - Make the code changes required
   - Keep changes minimal and focused
   - Mark task complete in the tasks file: `- [ ]` → `- [x]`
   - Continue to next task

   **Pause if:**
   - Task is unclear → ask for clarification
   - Implementation reveals a design issue → suggest updating artifacts
   - Error or blocker encountered → report and wait for guidance
   - User interrupts

7. **On completion or pause, show status**

   Display:
   - Tasks completed this session
   - Overall progress: "N/M tasks complete"
   - If all done: suggest archive
   - If paused: explain why and wait for guidance

**Guardrails**
- Keep going through tasks until done or blocked
- Always read context files before starting (from the apply instructions output)
- If task is ambiguous, pause and ask before implementing
- If implementation reveals issues, pause and suggest artifact updates
- Keep code changes minimal and scoped to each task
- Update task checkbox immediately after completing each task
- Pause on errors, blockers, or unclear requirements - don't guess
- Use contextFiles from CLI output, don't assume specific file names

**Fluid Workflow Integration**

This skill supports the "actions on a change" model:

- **Can be invoked anytime**: Before all artifacts are done (if tasks exist), after partial implementation, interleaved with other actions
- **Allows artifact updates**: If implementation reveals design issues, suggest updating artifacts - not phase-locked, work fluidly
````

### Tool Call [completed]: packages/mimo-platform/src/projects/routes.tsx

**Tool:** read
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:24:39
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/packages/mimo-platform/src/projects/routes.tsx

```
<path>/home/bit4bit/src/mimo/packages/mimo-platform/src/projects/routes.tsx</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>1: import { Hono } from "hono";
2: import { projectRepository, CreateProjectInput } from "../projects/repository";
3: import { sessionRepository } from "../sessions/repository";
4: import { credentialRepository, Credential } from "../credentials/repository";
5: import { impactRepository } from "../impact/repository";
6: import { authMiddleware } from "../auth/middleware";
7: import { ProjectsListPage } from "../components/ProjectsListPage";
8: import { ProjectDetailPage } from "../components/ProjectDetailPage";
9: import { ProjectCreatePage } from "../components/ProjectCreatePage";
10: import { ProjectEditPage } from "../components/ProjectEditPage";
11: import { ImpactHistoryPage } from "../components/ImpactHistoryPage";
12: import sessions from "../sessions/routes";
13: 
14: const projects = new Hono();
15: 
16: // Helper to detect if URL is SSH
17: function isSshUrl(url: string): boolean {
18:   return url.startsWith("git@") || url.startsWith("ssh://");
19: }
20: 
21: // Helper to get credential type from URL
22: function getCredentialTypeFromUrl(url: string): "https" | "ssh" {
23:   return isSshUrl(url) ? "ssh" : "https";
24: }
25: 
26: // List all projects (GET /projects)
27: projects.get("/", authMiddleware, async (c) => {
28:   const user = c.get("user") as { username: string };
29:   const projectsList = await projectRepository.listByOwner(user.username);
30:   return c.html(<ProjectsListPage projects={projectsList} />);
31: });
32: 
33: // Show create form (GET /projects/new)
34: projects.get("/new", authMiddleware, async (c) => {
35:   const user = c.get("user") as { username: string };
36:   const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);
37:   return c.html(<ProjectCreatePage credentials={credentials} />);
38: });
39: 
40: // Create project (POST /projects)
41: projects.post("/", authMiddleware, async (c) => {
42:   const body = await c.req.parseBody();
43:   const name = body.name as string;
44:   const repoUrl = body.repoUrl as string;
45:   const repoType = (body.repoType as string) || "git";
46:   const description = body.description as string | undefined;
47:   const credentialId = body.credentialId as string | undefined;
48:   const sourceBranch = body.sourceBranch as string | undefined;
49:   const newBranch = body.newBranch as string | undefined;
50:   const defaultLocalDevMirrorPath = body.defaultLocalDevMirrorPath as string | undefined;
51:   const user = c.get("user") as { username: string };
52: 
53:   if (!name || !repoUrl) {
54:     const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);
55:     return c.html(<ProjectCreatePage credentials={credentials} error="Name and repository URL are required" />, 400);
56:   }
57: 
58:   // Validate URL format
59:   try {
60:     new URL(repoUrl);
61:   } catch {
62:     // Allow SSH URLs (git@github.com:user/repo.git)
63:     if (!isSshUrl(repoUrl)) {
64:       const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);
65:       return c.html(<ProjectCreatePage credentials={credentials} error="Invalid repository URL" />, 400);
66:     }
67:   }
68: 
69:   // Validate repo type
70:   if (repoType !== "git" && repoType !== "fossil") {
71:     const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);
72:     return c.html(<ProjectCreatePage credentials={credentials} error="Repository type must be 'git' or 'fossil'" />, 400);
73:   }
74: 
75:   // Validate description length
76:   if (description && description.length > 500) {
77:     const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);
78:     return c.html(<ProjectCreatePage credentials={credentials} error="Description must be 500 characters or less" />, 400);
79:   }
80: 
81:   // Validate credential if provided
82:   if (credentialId) {
83:     const credential = await credentialRepository.findById(credentialId, user.username);
84:     if (!credential) {
85:       const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);
86:       return c.html(<ProjectCreatePage credentials={credentials} error="Selected credential not found" />, 400);
87:     }
88:     
89:     // Validate credential type matches URL type
90:     const expectedType = getCredentialTypeFromUrl(repoUrl);
91:     if (credential.type !== expectedType) {
92:       const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);
93:       return c.html(
94:         <ProjectCreatePage 
95:           credentials={credentials} 
96:           error={`Credential type does not match repository URL type. Expected ${expectedType.toUpperCase()} but got ${credential.type.toUpperCase()}`} 
97:         />, 
98:         400
99:       );
100:     }
101:   }
102:   
103:   try {
104:     const project = await projectRepository.create({
105:       name,
106:       repoUrl,
107:       repoType: repoType as "git" | "fossil",
108:       owner: user.username,
109:       description: description || undefined,
110:       credentialId: credentialId || undefined,
111:       sourceBranch: sourceBranch || undefined,
112:       newBranch: newBranch || undefined,
113:       defaultLocalDevMirrorPath: defaultLocalDevMirrorPath || undefined,
114:     });
115: 
116:     return c.redirect(`/projects/${project.id}`, 302);
117:   } catch (error) {
118:     const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);
119:     return c.html(<ProjectCreatePage credentials={credentials} error="Failed to create project" />, 500);
120:   }
121: });
122: 
123: // View project (GET /projects/:id)
124: projects.get("/:id", authMiddleware, async (c) => {
125:   const id = c.req.param("id");
126:   const project = await projectRepository.findById(id);
127:   
128:   if (!project) {
129:     return c.notFound();
130:   }
131: 
132:   const user = c.get("user") as { username: string };
133:   if (project.owner !== user.username) {
134:     return c.notFound();
135:   }
136: 
137:   // Load credential info if exists
138:   let credential: Credential | null = null;
139:   if (project.credentialId) {
140:     credential = await credentialRepository.findById(project.credentialId, user.username);
141:   }
142: 
143:   const sessions = await sessionRepository.listByProject(id);
144: 
145:   return c.html(<ProjectDetailPage project={project} sessions={sessions} credential={credential} />);
146: });
147: 
148: // Edit project form (GET /projects/:id/edit)
149: projects.get("/:id/edit", authMiddleware, async (c) => {
150:   const id = c.req.param("id");
151:   const project = await projectRepository.findById(id);
152:   
153:   if (!project) {
154:     return c.notFound();
155:   }
156: 
157:   const user = c.get("user") as { username: string };
158:   if (project.owner !== user.username) {
159:     return c.notFound();
160:   }
161: 
162:   const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);
163:   return c.html(<ProjectEditPage project={project} credentials={credentials} />);
164: });
165: 
166: // Update project (POST /projects/:id/edit)
167: projects.post("/:id/edit", authMiddleware, async (c) => {
168:   const id = c.req.param("id");
169:   const project = await projectRepository.findById(id);
170:   
171:   if (!project) {
172:     return c.notFound();
173:   }
174: 
175:   const user = c.get("user") as { username: string };
176:   if (project.owner !== user.username) {
177:     return c.notFound();
178:   }
179: 
180:   const body = await c.req.parseBody();
181:   const name = body.name as string;
182:   const repoUrl = body.repoUrl as string;
183:   const repoType = (body.repoType as string) || "git";
184:   const description = body.description as string | undefined;
185:   const credentialId = body.credentialId as string | undefined;
186:   const defaultLocalDevMirrorPath = body.defaultLocalDevMirrorPath as string | undefined;
187: 
188:   if (!name || !repoUrl) {
189:     const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);
190:     return c.html(<ProjectEditPage project={project} credentials={credentials} error="Name and repository URL are required" />, 400);
191:   }
192: 
193:   // Validate URL format
194:   try {
195:     new URL(repoUrl);
196:   } catch {
197:     if (!isSshUrl(repoUrl)) {
198:       const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);
199:       return c.html(<ProjectEditPage project={project} credentials={credentials} error="Invalid repository URL" />, 400);
200:     }
201:   }
202: 
203:   // Validate repo type
204:   if (repoType !== "git" && repoType !== "fossil") {
205:     const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);

207:   }
208: 
209:   // Validate description length
210:   if (description && description.length > 500) {
211:     const credentials = await credentialRepository.findByOwner(user.username);
212:     return c.html(<ProjectEditPage project={project} credentials={credentials} error="Description must be 500 characters or less" />, 400);
213:   }

235:     }

247:

249:   } catch (error) {
250:     const errorMessage = error instanceof Error ? error.message : "Failed to update project";
```

### Tool Call [completed]: packages/mimo-platform/src/projects/routes.tsx

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:24:47

oldString: // Delete project (POST /projects/:id/delete)
projects.post("/:id/delete", authMiddleware, async (c) => {
newString: // Freeze project (POST /projects/:id/freeze)
projects.post("/:id/freeze", authMiddleware, async (c) => {
  const id = c.req.param("id");
  const project = await projectRepository.findById(id);
  
  if (!project) {
    return c.notFound();
  }

  const user = c.get("user") as { username: string };
  if (project.owner !== user.username) {
    return c.notFound();
  }

  // Get all sessions for this project and freeze them
  const sessions = await sessionRepository.listByProject(id);
  for (const session of sessions) {
    await sessionRepository.update(session.id, { status: "frozen" });
  }

  return c.redirect(`/projects/${id}`, 302);
});

// Delete project (POST /projects/:id/delete)
projects.post("/:id/delete", authMiddleware, async (c) => {

```
4: 
5: export interface ChatMessage {
6:   role: "user" | "assistant" | "system";
7:   content: string;
8:   timestamp: string;
9:   metadata?: Record<string, unknown>;
10: }
11: 
12: export class ChatService {
13:   private getChatPath(sessionId: string): string {
14:     // Store chat in the session directory
15:     const Paths = getPaths();
16:     const sessionDir = this.findSessionDir(sessionId);
17:     if (!sessionDir) {
18:       throw new Error(`Session ${sessionId} not found`);
19:     }
20:     return join(sessionDir, "chat.jsonl");
21:   }
22: 
23:   private findSessionDir(sessionId: string): string | null {
24:     const Paths = getPaths();
25:     if (!existsSync(Paths.projects)) {
26:       return null;
27:     }
28: 
29:     const { readdirSync } = require("fs");
30:     const projectEntries = readdirSync(Paths.projects, { withFileTypes: true });
31:     
32:     for (const projectEntry of projectEntries) {
33:       if (projectEntry.isDirectory()) {
34:         const sessionsDir = join(Paths.projects, projectEntry.name, "sessions");
35:         if (existsSync(sessionsDir)) {
36:           const sessionDir = join(sessionsDir, sessionId);
37:           if (existsSync(sessionDir)) {
38:             return sessionDir;
39:           }
40:         }
41:       }
42:     }
43: 
44:     return null;
45:   }
46: 
47:   async saveMessage(sessionId: string, message: ChatMessage): Promise<void> {
48:     const chatPath = this.getChatPath(sessionId);
49:     const line = JSON.stringify(message) + "\n";
50:     appendFileSync(chatPath, line, "utf-8");
51:   }
52: 
53:   async loadHistory(sessionId: string): Promise<ChatMessage[]> {
54:     try {
55:       const chatPath = this.getChatPath(sessionId);
56:       if (!existsSync(chatPath)) {
57:         return [];
58:       }
59: 
60:       const content = readFileSync(chatPath, "utf-8");
61:       const lines = content.trim().split("\n").filter(line => line);
62:       
63:       return lines.map((line) => JSON.parse(line) as ChatMessage);
64:     } catch {
65:       return [];
66:     }
67:   }
68: 
69:   async appendToHistory(sessionId: string, messages: ChatMessage[]): Promise<void> {
70:     const chatPath = this.getChatPath(sessionId);
71:     const lines = messages.map((msg) => JSON.stringify(msg)).join("\n") + "\n";
72:     appendFileSync(chatPath, lines, "utf-8");
73:   }
74: 
75:   async clearHistory(sessionId: string): Promise<void> {
76:     const chatPath = this.getChatPath(sessionId);
77:     if (existsSync(chatPath)) {
78:       const { unlinkSync } = require("fs");
79:       unlinkSync(chatPath);
80:     }
81:   }
82: }
83: 
84: export const chatService = new ChatService();
```

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 22:28:50)

## Implementation Complete

**Change:** project-freeze
**Schema:** spec-driven
**Progress:** 17/17 tasks complete ✓

### Summary of Changes

**1. Session Status Type** (packages/mimo-platform/src/sessions/repository.ts)
- Added `frozen` to Session and SessionData status enum
- Status now supports: `"active" | "paused" | "closed" | "frozen"`

**2. Project Freeze Action** (packages/mimo-platform/src/projects/routes.tsx)
- Created POST route handler for `/projects/:id/freeze`
- Iterates all project sessions and updates status to `frozen`
- Redirects back to project detail page

**3. Block Chat Messages** (packages/mimo-platform/src/index.tsx)
- Added status check in `handleChatMessage` for `send_message` type
- Returns error message and exits early if session is frozen
- Reuses existing session lookup to avoid double query

**4. Block Commits** (packages/mimo-platform/src/commits/service.ts)
- Added status check at start of `commitAndPush` method
- Returns error with message "Session is frozen. Cannot commit changes."

**5. UI Updates**
- ProjectDetailPage.tsx: Added "Freeze Project" button in Actions section, updated Session interface
- SessionListPage.tsx: Updated Session interface to include `frozen` status

All tasks complete! Ready to archive this change.## User (2026-04-08 22:29:32)

### Tool Call [completed]: packages/mimo-platform/test/sessions.test.ts

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:31:39
**Parameters:**
oldString:     });
  });

newString:     });
  });

  describe("Session Freeze", () => {
    it("should update session status to frozen", async () => {
      await userRepository.create("testuser", await bcrypt.hash("testpass", 10));
      const project = await projectRepository.create({
        name: "Test Project",
        repoUrl: "https://github.com/user/repo.git",
        repoType: "git",
        owner: "testuser",
      });

      const session = await sessionRepository.create({
        name: "Session To Freeze",
        projectId: project.id,
        owner: "testuser",
      });

      expect(session.status).toBe("active");

      const updated = await sessionRepository.update(session.id, { status: "frozen" });
      expect(updated?.status).toBe("frozen");
    });

    it("should freeze all sessions when project freeze action is invoked", async () => {
      const app = new Hono();
      app.route("/projects/:projectId/sessions", sessionRoutes);

      // Need to mount project routes for freeze endpoint
      const projectsModule = await import("../src/projects/routes.tsx");
      const projectRoutes = projectsModule.default;
      app.route("/projects", projectRoutes);

      await userRepository.create("testuser", await bcrypt.hash("testpass", 10));
      const project = await projectRepository.create({
        name: "Test Project",
        repoUrl: "https://github.com/user/repo.git",
        repoType: "git",
        owner: "testuser",
      });

      // Create 3 sessions
      await sessionRepository.create({
        name: "Session 1",
        projectId: project.id,
        owner: "testuser",
      });
      await sessionRepository.create({
        name: "Session 2",
        projectId: project.id,
        owner: "testuser",
      });
      await sessionRepository.create({
        name: "Session 3",
        projectId: project.id,
        owner: "testuser",
      });

      const token = await generateToken("testuser");

      // Call freeze endpoint
      const res = await app.request(`/projects/${project.id}/freeze`, {
        method: "POST",
        headers: { Cookie: `token=${token}` },
      });

      expect(res.status).toBe(302);

      // Verify all sessions are frozen
      const sessions = await sessionRepository.listByProject(project.id);
      expect(sessions.length).toBe(3);
      sessions.forEach((s) => {
        expect(s.status).toBe("frozen");
      });
    });

    it("should return 404 for freeze on non-existent project", async () => {
      const app = new Hono();
      const projectsModule = await import("../src/projects/routes.tsx");
      const projectRoutes = projectsModule.default;
      app.route("/projects", projectRoutes);

      await userRepository.create("testuser", await bcrypt.hash("testpass", 10));
      const token = await generateToken("testuser");

      const res = await app.request(`/projects/non-existent-id/freeze`, {
        method: "POST",
        headers: { Cookie: `token=${token}` },
      });

      expect(res.status).toBe(404);
    });

    it("should handle freeze on project with no sessions", async () => {
      const app = new Hono();
      const projectsModule = await import("../src/projects/routes.tsx");
      const projectRoutes = projectsModule.default;
      app.route("/projects", projectRoutes);

      await userRepository.create("testuser", await bcrypt.hash("testpass", 10));
      const project = await projectRepository.create({
        name: "Empty Project",
        repoUrl: "https://github.com/user/repo.git",
        repoType: "git",
        owner: "testuser",
      });

      const token = await generateToken("testuser");

      const res = await app.request(`/projects/${project.id}/freeze`, {
        method: "POST",
        headers: { Cookie: `token=${token}` },
      });

      expect(res.status).toBe(302);

      // Verify no sessions exist
      const sessions = await sessionRepository.listByProject(project.id);
      expect(sessions.length).toBe(0);
    });
  });
});
