## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 22:31:47)

I see the commits test file. I should add a test for frozen session blocking commits. Let me add it:

### Tool Call [completed]: packages/mimo-platform/test/commits.test.ts

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:32:00
**Parameters:**
newString:       const result = await CommitService.commitAndPush(session.id);

      // When no changes, the service returns success=true with message "No changes to commit"
      // This is expected behavior - no changes is not an error
      expect(result.success).toBe(true);
      expect(result.message).toContain("No changes to commit");
    }, 30000);

    it("should block commit when session is frozen", async () => {
      const vcs = new VCS();
      const sessionRepo = new SessionRepository();
      const projectRepo = new ProjectRepository();

      // Create a project
      const project = await projectRepo.create({
        name: "Frozen Test Project",
        repoUrl: "https://github.com/test/repo.git",
        repoType: "git",
        owner: "testuser",
      });

      // Create a session
      const session = await sessionRepo.create({
        name: "Frozen Session",
        projectId: project.id,
        owner: "testuser",
      });

      // Freeze the session
      await sessionRepo.update(session.id, { status: "frozen" });

      // Try to commit
      const result = await CommitService.commitAndPush(session.id);

      expect(result.success).toBe(false);
      expect(result.message).toContain("frozen");
      expect(result.error).toBe("Session is frozen");
    });
  });
});
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/packages/mimo-platform/test/commits.test.ts

<content>730: 
731: // Handle chat messages
732: async function handleChatMessage(ws, data) {
733:   const sessionId = ws.data.sessionId;
734:   
735:   switch (data.type) {
736:     case "send_message":
737:       // Check if session is frozen
738:       const session = await sessionRepository.findById(sessionId);
739:       if (session?.status === "frozen") {
740:         ws.send(JSON.stringify({
741:           type: 'error',
742:           message: 'Session is frozen. Cannot send messages.',
743:         }));
744:         return;
745:       }
746:       
747:       // Save user message
748:       await chatService.saveMessage(sessionId, {
749:         role: 'user',
750:         content: data.content,
751:         timestamp: new Date().toISOString(),
752:       });
753: 
754:       // Broadcast to all clients in session
755:       const subscribers = chatSessions.get(sessionId);
756:       if (subscribers) {
757:         subscribers.forEach(client => {
758:           if (client.readyState === 1) {
759:             client.send(JSON.stringify({
760:               type: 'message',
761:               role: 'user',
762:               content: data.content,
763:               timestamp: new Date().toISOString(),
764:             }));
765:           }
766:         });
767:       }
768: 
769:       // Forward to agent if connected
770:       if (session?.assignedAgentId) {
771:         // Forward to agent if connected
772:         const ws = agentService.getAgentConnection(session.assignedAgentId);
773:         if (ws && ws.readyState === 1) {
774:           ws.send(JSON.stringify({
775:             type: 'user_message',
776:             sessionId: sessionId,
777:             content: data.content,
778:           }));
779:         }
780:       }
781:       break;
782: 
783:     case "set_model":
784:       // Forward model change to agent
785:       const modelSession = await sessionRepository.findById(sessionId);
786:       if (modelSession?.assignedAgentId) {
787:         const agentWs = agentService.getAgentConnection(modelSession.assignedAgentId);
788:         if (agentWs && agentWs.readyState === 1) {
789:           agentWs.send(JSON.stringify({
790:             type: 'set_model',
791:             sessionId: sessionId,
792:             modelId: data.modelId,
793:           }));
794:         }
795:       }
796:       break;
797: 
798:     case "set_mode":
799:       // Forward mode change to agent
800:       const modeSession = await sessionRepository.findById(sessionId);
801:       if (modeSession?.assignedAgentId) {
802:         const modeAgentWs = agentService.getAgentConnection(modeSession.assignedAgentId);
803:         if (modeAgentWs && modeAgentWs.readyState === 1) {
804:           modeAgentWs.send(JSON.stringify({
805:             type: 'set_mode',
806:             sessionId: sessionId,
807:             modeId: data.modeId,
808:           }));
809:         }

240:           function formatTrend(current, previous) {
241:             if (current > previous) return '↑';
242:             if (current < previous) return '↓';

252:             if (minutes < 60) return minutes + 'm';
253:             const hours = Math.floor(minutes / 60);

255:             return hours + 'h ' + mins + 'm';

261:               if (!response.ok) throw new Error('Failed to fetch impact');

272:             if (!content) return;

322:             }

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 22:35:32)

I found the issue! There's an HTTP fallback route at `POST /sessions/:id/chat` that doesn't check for frozen status. Let me add the check there.

### Tool Call [completed]: packages/mimo-platform/src/sessions/routes.tsx

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:35:42
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/packages/mimo-platform/src/sessions/routes.tsx
oldString: // POST /sessions/:id/chat - Save a chat message
router.post("/:id/chat", async (c: Context) => {
  const username = await getAuthUsername(c);
  if (!username) {
    return c.redirect("/auth/login");
  }

  const sessionId = c.req.param("id");
  const session = await sessionRepository.findById(sessionId);

  if (!session || session.owner !== username) {
    return c.text("Session not found", 404);
  }

  const body = await c.req.parseBody();
  const message = body.message as string;

  if (!message) {
    return c.text("Message required", 400);
  }

  await chatService.saveMessage(sessionId, {
    role: "user",
    content: message,
    timestamp: new Date().toISOString(),
  });

  return c.json({ success: true });
});
newString: // POST /sessions/:id/chat - Save a chat message
router.post("/:id/chat", async (c: Context) => {
  const username = await getAuthUsername(c);
  if (!username) {
    return c.redirect("/auth/login");
  }

  const sessionId = c.req.param("id");
  const session = await sessionRepository.findById(sessionId);

  if (!session || session.owner !== username) {
    return c.text("Session not found", 404);
  }

  // Check if session is frozen
  if (session.status === "frozen") {
    return c.text("Session is frozen. Cannot send messages.", 403);
  }

  const body = await c.req.parseBody();
  const message = body.message as string;

  if (!message) {
    return c.text("Message required", 400);
  }

  await chatService.saveMessage(sessionId, {
    role: "user",
    content: message,
    timestamp: new Date().toISOString(),
  });

  return c.json({ success: true });
});

```

    it("should block HTTP chat messages when session is frozen", async () => {
      const app = new Hono();
      app.route("/projects/:projectId/sessions", sessionRoutes);

      await userRepository.create("testuser", await bcrypt.hash("testpass", 10));
      const project = await projectRepository.create({
        name: "Test Project",
        repoUrl: "https://github.com/user/repo.git",
        repoType: "git",
        owner: "testuser",
      });

      const session = await sessionRepository.create({
        name: "Frozen Session",
        projectId: project.id,
        owner: "testuser",
      });

      // Freeze the session
      await sessionRepository.update(session.id, { status: "frozen" });

      const token = await generateToken("testuser");

      // Try to send HTTP chat message
      const res = await app.request(`/projects/${project.id}/sessions/${session.id}/chat`, {
        method: "POST",
        headers: {
          "Content-Type": "application/x-www-form-urlencoded",
          Cookie: `token=${token}`,
        },
        body: new URLSearchParams({ message: "Hello" }).toString(),
      });

      expect(res.status).toBe(403);
      const text = await res.text();
      expect(text).toContain("frozen");
    });
  });
});

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 22:37:37)

The chat input is handled dynamically by JavaScript in `chat.js`. The server doesn't render an input box directly - it's created client-side.

To disable the input for frozen sessions, I have a few options:

1. **Server-side**: Pass the frozen status to the page and have JavaScript disable the input
2. **Client-side**: JavaScript fetches session status and disables input if frozen
3. **Simplest**: Pass `isFrozen` flag to SessionDetailPage and let the JavaScript handle it

Actually, looking at the chat.js, the editable bubble is created dynamically. I need to either:
1. Pass a data attribute or global variable indicating frozen status
2. Have the JavaScript check session status on load

Let me look at how chat.js gets the session ID - it probably extracts it from the URL or a data attribute.

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 22:39:20)

I can see the `createEditableBubble` function. I need to check if the session is frozen when creating the bubble and also when submitting. Let me modify the `createEditableBubble` function to disable editing when frozen:

### Tool Call [completed]: packages/mimo-platform/public/js/chat.js

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:39:43
**Parameters:**
newString:   // Create the editable YOU bubble at the bottom of chat-messages
  function createEditableBubble() {
    const chatContainer = document.querySelector('#chat-messages');
    if (!chatContainer) return;
    // Don't create if one already exists
    if (editableBubble) return;

    // Check if session is frozen
    const isFrozen = window.MIMO_SESSION_STATUS === 'frozen';

    const bubble = document.createElement('div');
    bubble.className = 'message message-user editable-bubble';

    // Header: YOU · ● status · spacer · [⌃↵ Send]
    const header = document.createElement('div');
    header.className = 'message-header editable-bubble-header';

    const label = document.createElement('span');
    label.textContent = 'You';

    const status = document.createElement('span');
    status.className = 'editable-bubble-status';
    status.title = 'Connection status';

    const spacer = document.createElement('span');
    spacer.style.flex = '1';

    const sendBtn = document.createElement('button');
    sendBtn.type = 'button';
    sendBtn.className = 'editable-send-btn';
    sendBtn.textContent = isFrozen ? 'Session Frozen' : '\u2318\u21b5 Send';
    sendBtn.disabled = isFrozen;
    if (!isFrozen) {
      sendBtn.addEventListener('click', submitEditableBubble);
    }

    header.appendChild(label);
    header.appendChild(status);
    header.appendChild(spacer);
    header.appendChild(sendBtn);

    // Editable content area
    const content = document.createElement('div');
    content.className = 'message-content';
    content.contentEditable = isFrozen ? 'false' : 'true';
    content.setAttribute('data-placeholder', isFrozen ? 'Session is frozen. Cannot send messages.' : 'Type a message...');

    if (!isFrozen) {
      // Ctrl+Enter to send; Enter inserts newline (native contenteditable behavior)
      content.addEventListener('keydown', (e) => {
        if (e.key === 'Enter' && e.ctrlKey) {
          e.preventDefault();
          submitEditableBubble();
        }
      });

      // Paste: strip HTML, insert plain text only
      content.addEventListener('paste', (e) => {
        e.preventDefault();
        const text = e.clipboardData.getData('text/plain');
        document.execCommand('insertText', false, text);
      });
    }

    bubble.appendChild(header);
    bubble.appendChild(content);

    chatContainer.appendChild(bubble);
    scrollToBottom();
    if (!isFrozen) {
      content.focus();
    }

    editableBubble = bubble;

    // Apply current connection status to the new bubble
    showConnectionStatus(_lastConnectionStatus || 'disconnected');
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/packages/mimo-platform/public/js/chat.js

  function createEditableBubble() {
    const chatContainer = document.querySelector('#chat-messages');
    if (!chatContainer) return;
    // Don't create if one already exists
    if (editableBubble) return;

    const bubble = document.createElement('div');
    bubble.className = 'message message-user editable-bubble';

    // Header: YOU · ● status · spacer · [⌃↵ Send]
    const header = document.createElement('div');
    header.className = 'message-header editable-bubble-header';

    const label = document.createElement('span');

    const status = document.createElement('span');
    status.className = 'editable-bubble-status';

    const spacer = document.createElement('span');
    spacer.style.flex = '1';

    chatContainer.appendChild(bubble);
    scrollToBottom();
    content.focus();

    editableBubble = bubble;

    // Apply current connection status to the new bubble
    showConnectionStatus(_lastConnectionStatus || 'disconnected');

+    if (!isFrozen) {
+      content.focus();
+    }
 
     editableBubble = bubble;

### Tool Call [completed]: Loaded skill: llm-vcs-session-saver

**Tool:** other
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:40:33
**Parameters:**
name: llm-vcs-session-saver

````
<skill_content name="llm-vcs-session-saver">
# Skill: llm-vcs-session-saver

# LLM VCS Session Saver

Saves an LLM conversation session as a flat text file optimized for version control: one line per message, unique timestamped filename, no identifying information. Works with any VCS — Git, SVN, Mercurial, Perforce, and others.

---

## Output File Path

Save the session file to:

```
llm-sessions/YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS-XXXX-session.txt
```

- `YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS` — timestamp of when the session was saved (UTC)
- `XXXX` — 4-character random alphanumeric string to prevent collisions
- Do **not** include usernames, email addresses, or any identifying info in the filename or content

Example: `llm-sessions/2025-04-01-143022-k7qr-session.txt`

---

## Content Format

Each message must be written as a **single line** in this exact format:

```
[YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS] User: <message text>
[YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS] LLM: <message text>
```

### Rules

- **Chronological order** — messages appear in the order they occurred
- **Timestamps** — use `YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS` format (UTC preferred)
- **Speaker labels** — only `User:` and `LLM:` (no other labels or roles)
- **One line per message** — newlines within a message must be replaced with a space or `\n` literal so each message stays on one line
- **No summarizing** — reproduce messages fully and verbatim
- **No extra formatting** — no markdown, no section headers, no blank lines between messages
- **No metadata block** — do not prepend titles, model names, or session IDs

### Example Output

```
[2025-04-01 14:30:01] User: What is the capital of France?
[2025-04-01 14:30:03] LLM: The capital of France is Paris.
[2025-04-01 14:30:10] User: And what's the population?
[2025-04-01 14:30:12] LLM: Paris has a population of approximately 2.1 million in the city proper.
```

---

## Git Readiness

- The file can be written directly and committed with no post-processing
- One-line-per-message ensures Git diffs are clean and human-readable — each changed message shows as exactly one modified line
- The `llm-sessions/` directory should be committed as part of the repo (not gitignored)

---

## Commit Workflow

Every time the user asks to make a Git commit — for any reason, even if unrelated to sessions — run this skill first, then include the session file in the commit.

Steps to follow on every commit:

1. **Generate the session file** using the path format and content rules above
2. **Stage the session file** along with the user's other changes:
   ```bash
   git add llm-sessions/YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS-XXXX-session.txt
   git add <any other files the user wants to commit>
   ```
3. **Commit everything together**:
   ```bash
   git commit -m "<user's commit message>"
   ```

The session file should reflect the full conversation up to and including the commit request itself.

---

## Multi-Session Safety

- Filenames are unique by design (timestamp + random ID), so concurrent sessions will never overwrite each other
- No locking or coordination needed between sessions
- If two sessions start in the same second, the random suffix (`XXXX`) prevents collision

Base directory for this skill: file:///home/bit4bit/.config/opencode/skills/session-history
Relative paths in this skill (e.g., scripts/, reference/) are relative to this base directory.
Note: file list is sampled.

<skill_files>

</skill_files>
</skill_content>
````

i made changes to the upstream repository but i can't force the pull -i want to force a pull replacing with the external changes - when i force a pull the current session need to be readonly only, not allowed more interaction.
[2025-04-08 23:33:05] LLM: I'm in explore mode. Let's think through this...

So you want to **force a pull from upstream** (external changes) and have the **current session become read-only** afterward. No more interaction allowed.

This feels like a **state synchronization + session lifecycle** problem. Let me understand the context better.

Now I see! This is MIMO - the web-based editor with sessions. You're working with **sessions** that have an `upstream/` directory containing a clone of the repository.

Let me trace through what you're describing:

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    SESSION LIFECYCLE                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

     External Repo                    Your Session
          │                              │
          │                              │
    ┌─────┴─────┐                  ┌─────┴─────┐
    │  ORIGIN   │                  │ UPSTREAM  │
    │  (live)   │◀─────────────────│  (clone)  │
    └─────┬─────┘                  └─────┬─────┘
          │                              │
          │                              ▼
          │                        ┌─────────────┐
          │                        │AGENT-WORKSP │
          │                        │  (edits)    │
          └───────────────────────▶│             │
              push changes         └─────────────┘
```

You're saying: **"I made changes to ORIGIN externally, and I want to force my session to pull those changes and then become read-only."**

A few directions this could go:

**1. The "Rescue Sync" scenario**
You were working, stepped away, someone else pushed to origin, now your session is out of sync. You want to abandon your session's state and match origin, then lock it so you don't accidentally overwrite.

**2. The "Archive" scenario**  
This session is done, but you want one last sync with upstream before freezing it forever.

**3. The "Conflict Avoidance" scenario**
You know there are upstream changes that will conflict with your session. You want to see them without risking accidental commits.

Which resonates? Or is it something else entirely?

Also curious: **Why read-only?** Is this about preventing accidental edits, or is it more about signaling "this session is finished"?

The implementation could be as simple as a flag in `session.yaml`:
```yaml
status: readonly  # or locked, frozen, etc.
```

But the *why* shapes the *what* here. What's driving this need?
[2025-04-08 23:33:10] User: you are wrong, i can have multiple session for the same project, but since a session have a stale project, i want to make it readonly.
[2025-04-08 23:33:15] LLM: Ah, I see! I was conflating the session's `upstream/` with the project's state. Let me re-trace this...

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              MULTI-SESSION PROJECT ARCHITECTURE            │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

External Repo
     │
     │ (clone at project creation)
     ▼
┌────────────┐         Session A (created Monday)     Session B (created Wednesday)
│  PROJECT   │         ┌───────────────┐              ┌───────────────┐
│  original/ │         │ upstream/     │              │ upstream/     │
│  (latest)  │         │ (Monday's     │              │ (Wednesday's  │
└────────────┘         │  state)       │              │  state)       │
     ▲                 └───────────────┘              └───────────────┘
     │                         │                              │
     │                         ▼                              ▼
     │                  agent-workspace/                 agent-workspace/
     │                  (editing...)                     (editing...)
     │
     │ (external push happens Thursday)
     ▼
  STALE! ───────────────► Session A and B are now behind

```

So each session is essentially a **point-in-time snapshot** of the external repo. When the external repo moves forward, those sessions become stale. You want to:

1. **Detect staleness** - Compare session's upstream commit with external HEAD
2. **Mark as read-only** - Prevent edits on stale sessions
3. **Visual indicator** - Show in UI that session is outdated

**A few paths to explore:**

**Option A: Lazy Detection**
Check staleness when session is opened. If behind → mark readonly.

**Option B: Proactive Polling**  
Background job checks all sessions periodically.

**Option C: Event-Driven**
Webhook/trigger when external repo changes (if you have push access to configure hooks).

**Option D: User-Initiated**
"Check for updates" button that user clicks, system compares and locks stale sessions.

Which feels right? Or is this triggered by something specific - like when the *project* itself pulls/fetches from external?

Also: When a session goes readonly, what should happen to the agent-workspace? Is it:
- Frozen (kept as-is for reference)?
- Cleared (can't do anything anyway)?
- Something else?
[2025-04-08 23:33:20] User: Option E, eager, i want when i force the update search for all the session and make it readonly.
agent-work just frozen
[2025-04-08 23:33:25] LLM: Got it. **Option E: Eager invalidation on force update.**

When you force-pull the project, all sessions immediately become readonly. Clean, deterministic, no surprises.

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              EAGER SESSION INVALIDATION FLOW                 │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

                         User Action
                            │
                            ▼
                   ┌────────────────┐
                   │  FORCE PULL    │
                   │ "Replace project│
│  with external" │
                   └───────┬────────┘
                           │
              ┌────────────┼────────────┐
              ▼            ▼            ▼
        ┌─────────┐   ┌─────────┐   ┌─────────┐
        │Session A│   │Session B│   │Session C│
        │ ACTIVE  │   │ ACTIVE  │   │ ACTIVE  │
        └────┬────┘   └────┬────┘   └────┬────┘
             │             │             │
             └─────────────┼─────────────┘
                           ▼
                   ┌────────────────┐
                   │  MARK ALL      │
                   │  READONLY      │
                   │  + Freeze WS   │
                   └───────┬────────┘
                           │
              ┌────────────┼────────────┐
              ▼            ▼            ▼
        ┌─────────┐   ┌─────────┐   ┌─────────┐
        │   🔒    │   │   🔒    │   │   🔒    │
        │ READONLY│   │ READONLY│   │ READONLY│
        │ agent-ws│   │ agent-ws│   │ agent-ws│
        │ FROZEN  │   │ FROZEN  │   │ FROZEN  │
        └─────────┘   └─────────┘   └─────────┘
```

This creates a clear lifecycle:

```
SESSION STATES
══════════════

┌─────────┐    force pull     ┌─────────┐    resume?    ┌─────────┐
│ ACTIVE  │ ─────────────────▶ │READONLY │ ───────────▶ │ ACTIVE  │
│ (edit)  │   project update   │ (view)  │   new pull   │ (edit)  │
└─────────┘                    └─────────┘              └─────────┘
      │                              │
      │ user closes                  │ user closes
      ▼                              ▼
┌─────────┐                    ┌─────────┐
│ARCHIVED │                    │ARCHIVED │
└─────────┘                    └─────────┘
```

**Key questions:**

1. **Status naming**: `"readonly"` or `"stale"` or `"frozen"`? I lean toward `"stale"` because it explains *why*.

2. **Freezing mechanism**: Should the file watcher just check status and refuse writes? Or also `chmod -R -w` on agent-workspace for extra safety?

3. **UI indicator**: Just a badge on the session? Or a full banner explaining "This session is stale - external changes detected"?

4. **What happens to running agents?** If Session A has an active agent process when force pull happens, should it be:
   - Killed immediately?
   - Allowed to finish current operation then shut down?
   - Just forbidden from making new file changes?

5. **Should force-pull be undoable?** Like a "restore previous state" option?

This feels like a solid, clean feature. Want me to capture this as an OpenSpec change so you can start implementing? Or keep exploring edge cases?

[2025-04-08 23:34:00] User: Fast-forward through artifact creation - generate everything needed to start implementation.

**Input**: The argument after `/opsx:ff` is the change name (kebab-case), OR a description of what the user wants to build.

**Steps**

1. **If no input provided, ask what they want to build**

   Use the **AskUserQuestion tool** (open-ended, no preset options) to ask:
   > "What change do you want to work on? Describe what you want to build or fix."

   From their description, derive a kebab-case name (e.g., "add user authentication" → `add-user-auth`).

   **IMPORTANT**: Do NOT proceed without understanding what the user wants to build.

2. **Create the change directory**
   ```bash
   openspec new change "<name>"
   ```
   This creates a scaffolded change at `openspec/changes/<name>/`.

3. **Get the artifact build order**
   ```bash
   openspec status --change "<name>" --json
   ```
   Parse the JSON to get:
   - `applyRequires`: array of artifact IDs needed before implementation (e.g., `["tasks"]`)
   - `artifacts`: list of all artifacts with their status and dependencies

4. **Create artifacts in sequence until apply-ready**

   Use the **TodoWrite tool** to track progress through the artifacts.

   Loop through artifacts in dependency order (artifacts with no pending dependencies first):

   a. **For each artifact that is `ready` (dependencies satisfied)**:
      - Get instructions:
        ```bash
        openspec instructions <artifact-id> --change "<name>" --json
        ```
      - The instructions JSON includes:
        - `context`: Project background (constraints for you - do NOT include in output)
        - `rules`: Artifact-specific rules (constraints for you - do NOT include in output)
        - `template`: The structure to use for your output file
        - `instruction`: Schema-specific guidance for this artifact type
        - `outputPath`: Where to write the artifact
        - `dependencies`: Completed artifacts to read for context
      - Read any completed dependency files for context
      - Create the artifact file using `template` as the structure
      - Apply `context` and `rules` as constraints - but do NOT copy them into the file
      - Show brief progress: "✓ Created <artifact-id>"

   b. **Continue until all `applyRequires` artifacts are complete**
      - After creating each artifact, re-run `openspec status --change "<name>" --json`
      - Check if every artifact ID in `applyRequires` has `status: "done"` in the artifacts array
      - Stop when all `applyRequires` artifacts are done

   c. **If an artifact requires user input** (unclear context):
      - Use **AskUserQuestion tool** to clarify
      - Then continue with creation

5. **Show final status**
   ```bash
   openspec status --change "<name>"
   ```

**Output**

After completing all artifacts, summarize:
- Change name and location
- List of artifacts created with brief descriptions
- What's ready: "All artifacts created! Ready for implementation."
- Prompt: "Run `/opsx:apply` to start implementing."

**Artifact Creation Guidelines**

- Follow the `instruction` field from `openspec instructions` for each artifact type
- The schema defines what each artifact should contain - follow it
- Read dependency artifacts before creating new ones
- Use the `template` as a starting point, filling in based on context

**Guardrails**
- Create ALL artifacts needed for implementation (as defined by schema's `apply.requires`)
- Always read dependency artifacts before creating a new one
- If context is critically unclear, ask the user - but prefer making reasonable decisions to keep momentum
- If a change with that name already exists, suggest continuing that change instead
- Verify each artifact file exists after writing before proceeding to next

+**IMPORTANT: Explore mode is for thinking, not implementing.** You may read files, search code, and investigate the codebase, but you must NEVER write code or implement features. You MAY create OpenSpec artifacts (proposals, designs, specs) if the user asks—that's capturing thinking, not implementing.
+
+**This is a stance, not a workflow.** There are no fixed steps, no required sequence, no mandatory outputs. You're a thinking partner helping the user explore.
+
+**Input**: The argument after `/opsx:explore` is whatever the user wants to think about. Could be:
+- A vague idea: "real-time collaboration"

+- A change name: "add-dark-mode" (to explore in context of that change)
+- A comparison: "postgres vs sqlite for this"

+## The Stance
+
+- **Curious, not prescriptive** - Ask questions that emerge naturally, don't follow a script
+- **Open threads, not interrogations** - Surface multiple interesting directions and let the user follow what resonates. Don't funnel them through a single path of questions.
+- **Visual** - Use ASCII diagrams liberally when they'd help clarify thinking
+- **Adaptive** - Follow interesting threads, pivot when new information emerges
+- **Patient** - Don't rush to conclusions, let the shape of the problem emerge
+- **Grounded** - Explore the actual codebase when relevant, don't just theorize
+
+---
+

+Depending on what the user brings, you might:

+i made changes to the upstream repository but i can't force the pull -i want to force a pull replacing with the external changes - when i force a pull the current session need to be readonly only, not allowed more interaction.
+[2025-04-08 23:33:05] LLM: I'm in explore mode. Let's think through this...
+
+So you want to **force a pull from upstream** (external changes) and have the **current session become read-only** afterward. No more interaction allowed.
+
+This feels like a **state synchronization + session lifecycle** problem. Let me understand the context better.
+
+Now I see! This is MIMO - the web-based editor with sessions. You're working with **sessions** that have an `upstream/` directory containing a clone of the repository.
+
+Let me trace through what you're describing:
+
+```
+┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
+│                    SESSION LIFECYCLE                         │
+└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
+
+     External Repo                    Your Session
+          │                              │
+          │                              │
+    ┌─────┴─────┐                  ┌─────┴─────┐
+    │  ORIGIN   │                  │ UPSTREAM  │
+    │  (live)   │◀─────────────────│  (clone)  │
+    └─────┬─────┘                  └─────┬─────┘
+          │                              │
+          │                              ▼
+          │                        ┌─────────────┐
+          │                        │AGENT-WORKSP │
+          │                        │  (edits)    │
+          └───────────────────────▶│             │
+              push changes         └─────────────┘
+```
+
+You're saying: **"I made changes to ORIGIN externally, and I want to force my session to pull those changes and then become read-only."**
+
+A few directions this could go:
+
+**1. The "Rescue Sync" scenario**
+You were working, stepped away, someone else pushed to origin, now your session is out of sync. You want to abandon your session's state and match origin, then lock it so you don't accidentally overwrite.
+
+**2. The "Archive" scenario**  
+This session is done, but you want one last sync with upstream before freezing it forever.
+
+**3. The "Conflict Avoidance" scenario**
+You know there are upstream changes that will conflict with your session. You want to see them without risking accidental commits.
+
+Which resonates? Or is it something else entirely?
+
+Also curious: **Why read-only?** Is this about preventing accidental edits, or is it more about signaling "this session is finished"?
+
+The implementation could be as simple as a flag in `session.yaml`:
+```yaml
+status: readonly  # or locked, frozen, etc.
+```
+
+But the *why* shapes the *what* here. What's driving this need?
+[2025-04-08 23:33:10] User: you are wrong, i can have multiple session for the same project, but since a session have a stale project, i want to make it readonly.
+[2025-04-08 23:33:15] LLM: Ah, I see! I was conflating the session's `upstream/` with the project's state. Let me re-trace this...
+
+```
+┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
+│              MULTI-SESSION PROJECT ARCHITECTURE            │
+└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
+
+External Repo
+     │
+     │ (clone at project creation)
+     ▼
+┌────────────┐         Session A (created Monday)     Session B (created Wednesday)
+│  PROJECT   │         ┌───────────────┐              ┌───────────────┐
+│  original/ │         │ upstream/     │              │ upstream/     │
+│  (latest)  │         │ (Monday's     │              │ (Wednesday's  │
+└────────────┘         │  state)       │              │  state)       │
+     ▲                 └───────────────┘              └───────────────┘
+     │                         │                              │
+     │                         ▼                              ▼
+     │                  agent-workspace/                 agent-workspace/
+     │                  (editing...)                     (editing...)
+     │
+     │ (external push happens Thursday)
+     ▼
+  STALE! ───────────────► Session A and B are now behind
+
+```
+
+So each session is essentially a **point-in-time snapshot** of the external repo. When the external repo moves forward, those sessions become stale. You want to:
+
+1. **Detect staleness** - Compare session's upstream commit with external HEAD
+2. **Mark as read-only** - Prevent edits on stale sessions
+3. **Visual indicator** - Show in UI that session is outdated
+
+**A few paths to explore:**
+
+**Option A: Lazy Detection**
+Check staleness when session is opened. If behind → mark readonly.
+
+**Option B: Proactive Polling**  
+Background job checks all sessions periodically.
+
+**Option C: Event-Driven**
+Webhook/trigger when external repo changes (if you have push access to configure hooks).
+
+**Option D: User-Initiated**
+"Check for updates" button that user clicks, system compares and locks stale sessions.
+
+Which feels right? Or is this triggered by something specific - like when the *project* itself pulls/fetches from external?
+
+Also: When a session goes readonly, what should happen to the agent-workspace? Is it:
+- Frozen (kept as-is for reference)?
+- Cleared (can't do anything anyway)?
+- Something else?
+[2025-04-08 23:33:20] User: Option E, eager, i want when i force the update search for all the session and make it readonly.
+agent-work just frozen
+[2025-04-08 23:33:25] LLM: Got it. **Option E: Eager invalidation on force update.**
+
+When you force-pull the project, all sessions immediately become readonly. Clean, deterministic, no surprises.
+
+```
+┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
+│              EAGER SESSION INVALIDATION FLOW                 │
+└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
+
+                         User Action
+                            │
+                            ▼
+                   ┌────────────────┐
+                   │  FORCE PULL    │
+                   │ "Replace project│
+│  with external" │
+                   └───────┬────────┘
+                           │
+              ┌────────────┼────────────┐
+              ▼            ▼            ▼
+        ┌─────────┐   ┌─────────┐   ┌─────────┐
+        │Session A│   │Session B│   │Session C│
+        │ ACTIVE  │   │ ACTIVE  │   │ ACTIVE  │
+        └────┬────┘   └────┬────┘   └────┬────┘
+             │             │             │
+             └─────────────┼─────────────┘
+                           ▼
+                   ┌────────────────┐
+                   │  MARK ALL      │
+                   │  READONLY      │
+                   │  + Freeze WS   │
+                   └───────┬────────┘
+                           │
+              ┌────────────┼────────────┐
+              ▼            ▼            ▼
+        ┌─────────┐   ┌─────────┐   ┌─────────┐
+        │   🔒    │   │   🔒    │   │   🔒    │
+        │ READONLY│   │ READONLY│   │ READONLY│
+        │ agent-ws│   │ agent-ws│   │ agent-ws│
+        │ FROZEN  │   │ FROZEN  │   │ FROZEN  │
+        └─────────┘   └─────────┘   └─────────┘
+```
+
+This creates a clear lifecycle:
+
+```
+SESSION STATES
+══════════════
+
+┌─────────┐    force pull     ┌─────────┐    resume?    ┌─────────┐
+│ ACTIVE  │ ─────────────────▶ │READONLY │ ───────────▶ │ ACTIVE  │
+│ (edit)  │   project update   │ (view)  │   new pull   │ (edit)  │
+└─────────┘                    └─────────┘              └─────────┘
+      │                              │
+      │ user closes                  │ user closes
+      ▼                              ▼
+┌─────────┐                    ┌─────────┐
+│ARCHIVED │                    │ARCHIVED │
+└─────────┘                    └─────────┘
+```
+
+**Key questions:**
+
+1. **Status naming**: `"readonly"` or `"stale"` or `"frozen"`? I lean toward `"stale"` because it explains *why*.
+
+2. **Freezing mechanism**: Should the file watcher just check status and refuse writes? Or also `chmod -R -w` on agent-workspace for extra safety?
+
+3. **UI indicator**: Just a badge on the session? Or a full banner explaining "This session is stale - external changes detected"?
+
+4. **What happens to running agents?** If Session A has an active agent process when force pull happens, should it be:
+   - Killed immediately?
+   - Allowed to finish current operation then shut down?
+   - Just forbidden from making new file changes?
+
+5. **Should force-pull be undoable?** Like a "restore previous state" option?
+
+This feels like a solid, clean feature. Want me to capture this as an OpenSpec change so you can start implementing? Or keep exploring edge cases?
+[2025-04-08 23:33:30] User: 1. frozen
+2. not need any change in agent-workspace
+3. good idea a badge
+4. not need any action
+5. not, not revert

+PROJECT DETAIL PAGE HEADER

+**Session list after freeze:**
+
+```
+SESSIONS
+════════
+
+┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
+│  Session Name    │  Created    │  Status  │  Actions            │

+│  refactor-db     │  2 weeks ago│ 🔒 FROZEN│ [View] [Archive]    │
+├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
+│  [+ New Session]                                                │
+└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
+```
+
+**What "frozen" prevents:**
+- File edits in agent-workspace (enforced by session status check)
+- Commits (commit button disabled)
+- Maybe: Starting new agents? Or allow it for viewing?
+
+**What frozen allows:**
+- Viewing chat history
+- Browsing files (read-only)
+- Running agents continue (no interruption)
+
+**Session status enum becomes:**
+```typescript
+status: "active" | "paused" | "closed" | "frozen"
+```

+│ └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │

+```
+
+**What this means:**
+
+| Can Do | Cannot Do |
+|--------|-----------|
+| Browse files | Send chat messages |
+| View chat history | Spawn new agents |
+| See current agent-workspace | |
+| Commit existing changes?* | |
+
+*Question: Can a user commit changes that were made **before** the freeze? Or does freeze also prevent commits?
+
+If the session already has uncommitted changes when frozen:
+- **Option A**: Allow commit (these are "clean up" commits)
+- **Option B**: Block commit (session is truly frozen, create new session to continue)

+[2025-04-08 23:34:00] User: Fast-forward through artifact creation - generate everything needed to start implementation.
+
+**Input**: The argument after `/opsx:ff` is the change name (kebab-case), OR a description of what the user wants to build.
+
+**Steps**
+
+1. **If no input provided, ask what they want to build**
+
+   Use the **AskUserQuestion tool** (open-ended, no preset options) to ask:
+   > "What change do you want to work on? Describe what you want to build or fix."
+
+   From their description, derive a kebab-case name (e.g., "add user authentication" → `add-user-auth`).
+
+   **IMPORTANT**: Do NOT proceed without understanding what the user wants to build.
+
+2. **Create the change directory**
+   ```bash
+   openspec new change "<name>"
+   ```
+   This creates a scaffolded change at `openspec/changes/<name>/`.
+
+3. **Get the artifact build order**
+   ```bash
+   openspec status --change "<name>" --json
+   ```
+   Parse the JSON to get:
+   - `applyRequires`: array of artifact IDs needed before implementation (e.g., `["tasks"]`)
+   - `artifacts`: list of all artifacts with their status and dependencies
+
+4. **Create artifacts in sequence until apply-ready**
+
+   Use the **TodoWrite tool** to track progress through the artifacts.
+
+   Loop through artifacts in dependency order (artifacts with no pending dependencies first):
+
+   a. **For each artifact that is `ready` (dependencies satisfied)**:
+      - Get instructions:
+        ```bash
+        openspec instructions <artifact-id> --change "<name>" --json
+        ```
+      - The instructions JSON includes:
+        - `context`: Project background (constraints for you - do NOT include in output)
+        - `rules`: Artifact-specific rules (constraints for you - do NOT include in output)
+        - `template`: The structure to use for your output file
+        - `instruction`: Schema-specific guidance for this artifact type
+        - `outputPath`: Where to write the artifact
+        - `dependencies`: Completed artifacts to read for context
+      - Read any completed dependency files for context
+      - Create the artifact file using `template` as the structure
+      - Apply `context` and `rules` as constraints - but do NOT copy them into the file
+      - Show brief progress: "✓ Created <artifact-id>"
+
+   b. **Continue until all `applyRequires` artifacts are complete**
+      - After creating each artifact, re-run `openspec status --change "<name>" --json`
+      - Check if every artifact ID in `applyRequires` has `status: "done"` in the artifacts array
+      - Stop when all `applyRequires` artifacts are done
+
+   c. **If an artifact requires user input** (unclear context):
+      - Use **AskUserQuestion tool** to clarify
+      - Then continue with creation
+
+5. **Show final status**
+   ```bash
+   openspec status --change "<name>"
+   ```
+
+**Output**
+
+After completing all artifacts, summarize:
+- Change name and location
+- List of artifacts created with brief descriptions
+- What's ready: "All artifacts created! Ready for implementation."
+- Prompt: "Run `/opsx:apply` to start implementing."
+
+**Artifact Creation Guidelines**
+
+- Follow the `instruction` field from `openspec instructions` for each artifact type
+- The schema defines what each artifact should contain - follow it
+- Read dependency artifacts before creating new ones
+- Use the `template` as a starting point, filling in based on context
+
+**Guardrails**
+- Create ALL artifacts needed for implementation (as defined by schema's `apply.requires`)
+- Always read dependency artifacts before creating a new one
+- If context is critically unclear, ask the user - but prefer making reasonable decisions to keep momentum
+- If a change with that name already exists, suggest continuing that change instead
+- Verify each artifact file exists after writing before proceeding to next

+2. **HTTP fallback** - Missing the frozen check ❌

+[2025-04-08 23:34:15] User: ok, but the user can write in the input box, can we avoid this?
+[2025-04-08 23:34:20] LLM: Yes! Let me disable the input box in the UI when the session is frozen.
+
+**What I changed to prevent typing in frozen sessions:**
+
+1. **Layout.tsx**: Pass `sessionStatus` to the window object via `window.MIMO_SESSION_STATUS`
+
+2. **SessionDetailPage.tsx**: Pass the session status to the Layout
+
+3. **chat.js**: When creating the editable bubble, check if session is frozen:
+   - Sets `contentEditable = 'false'`
+   - Disables the Send button
+   - Changes placeholder to "Session is frozen. Cannot send messages."
+   - Changes button text to "Session Frozen"
+   - Doesn't add keydown/paste event listeners
+   - Doesn't auto-focus
+
+Now when a user opens a frozen session, the chat input will be completely disabled - they can't type or send messages. The UI clearly shows it's frozen.

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 22:45:30)

The user is saying they misunderstood the feature they requested. They don't want to freeze the *project* - they want to pull remote changes to the project's upstream (original/), and only freeze *individual sessions* that are stale/outdated.

Let me visualize this:

Current implementation (wrong):
- User clicks "Freeze Project" 
- All sessions for that project become frozen
- Project itself doesn't change

What they actually want:
- Pull remote changes to project's `original/` (the upstream clone)
- Then freeze only sessions that are stale (have different state than the updated original/)

So the flow should be:
1. Project has an `original/` directory that is a clone of the external repo
2. User wants to pull latest changes from external repo into `original/`
3. After pulling, compare each session's `upstream/` with the updated `original/`
4. Sessions that are behind (stale) get frozen
5. Sessions that are up-to-date remain active

This makes more sense - you're refreshing the project's view of the external repo, and any sessions that were based on the old state become frozen.
## Agent (2026-04-08 22:45:35)

Ah, I see! The feature was inverted. Let me re-trace this...

```
CURRENT IMPLEMENTATION (Wrong)
═══════════════════════════════════════════

User clicks "Freeze Project"
         │
         ▼
┌────────────────┐
│ Mark ALL       │
│ sessions as    │──────► All sessions frozen (even current ones!)
│ frozen         │
└────────────────┘
         │
         ▼
   Project unchanged

WHAT YOU ACTUALLY WANT
═══════════════════════════════════════════

User clicks "Pull & Sync"
         │
         ▼
┌────────────────┐
│ Pull external  │
│ changes to     │──────► Project's original/ updated
│ project/orig/  │
└────────────────┘
         │
         ▼
┌────────────────┐
│ Compare each   │
│ session's      │
│ upstream with  │
│ updated        │
│ original       │
└────────────────┘
         │
    ┌────┴────┐
    ▼         ▼
┌──────┐  ┌──────┐
│STALE │  │CURRENT│
│session│  │session│
│  🔒  │  │  ✅   │
└──────┘  └──────┘
(frozen)  (active)
```

So the action is:
1. **Pull** external changes to project's `original/` directory
2. **Compare** each session's `upstream/` state with the updated `original/`
3. **Freeze only stale sessions** - ones that are behind the new external state

A few questions emerge:

**1. How do we detect staleness?**
- Compare git commits between session's `upstream/` and project's `original/`?
- Check if `original/` HEAD is ancestor of session's `upstream/` HEAD?
- Or just compare timestamps?

**2. What about the project page button?**
- Should it be "Pull & Sync" instead of "Freeze Project"?
- Or maybe two separate actions: "Pull Changes" (updates original/) and then auto-freeze stale sessions?

**3. What happens to active sessions that become frozen?**
- Should the UI immediately show them as frozen?
- Should there be a warning banner: "This session is now stale - external changes detected"?

**4. Can a user unfreeze a session?**
- Or do they just archive it and create a new one based on the updated project state?

This feels like a fundamentally different feature - more about **sync detection** than **bulk freeze**. The freeze is a side effect of staleness, not the primary action.

What are you thinking?

5: export interface ChatMessage {
6:   role: "user" | "assistant" | "system";
7:   content: string;
8:   timestamp: string;
9:   metadata?: Record<string, unknown>;
10: }
11: 
12: export class ChatService {
13:   private getChatPath(sessionId: string): string {
14:     // Store chat in the session directory
15:     const Paths = getPaths();
16:     const sessionDir = this.findSessionDir(sessionId);
17:     if (!sessionDir) {
18:       throw new Error(`Session ${sessionId} not found`);
19:     }
20:     return join(sessionDir, "chat.jsonl");
21:   }
22: 
23:   private findSessionDir(sessionId: string): string | null {
24:     const Paths = getPaths();
25:     if (!existsSync(Paths.projects)) {
26:       return null;
27:     }
28: 
29:     const { readdirSync } = require("fs");
30:     const projectEntries = readdirSync(Paths.projects, { withFileTypes: true });
31:     
32:     for (const projectEntry of projectEntries) {
33:       if (projectEntry.isDirectory()) {
34:         const sessionsDir = join(Paths.projects, projectEntry.name, "sessions");
35:         if (existsSync(sessionsDir)) {
36:           const sessionDir = join(sessionsDir, sessionId);
37:           if (existsSync(sessionDir)) {
38:             return sessionDir;
39:           }
40:         }
41:       }
42:     }
43: 
44:     return null;
45:   }
46: 
47:   async saveMessage(sessionId: string, message: ChatMessage): Promise<void> {
48:     const chatPath = this.getChatPath(sessionId);
49:     const line = JSON.stringify(message) + "\n";
50:     appendFileSync(chatPath, line, "utf-8");
51:   }
52: 
53:   async loadHistory(sessionId: string): Promise<ChatMessage[]> {
54:     try {
55:       const chatPath = this.getChatPath(sessionId);
56:       if (!existsSync(chatPath)) {
57:         return [];
58:       }
59: 
60:       const content = readFileSync(chatPath, "utf-8");
61:       const lines = content.trim().split("\n").filter(line => line);
62:       
63:       return lines.map((line) => JSON.parse(line) as ChatMessage);
64:     } catch {
65:       return [];
66:     }
67:   }
68: 
69:   async appendToHistory(sessionId: string, messages: ChatMessage[]): Promise<void> {
70:     const chatPath = this.getChatPath(sessionId);
71:     const lines = messages.map((msg) => JSON.stringify(msg)).join("\n") + "\n";
72:     appendFileSync(chatPath, lines, "utf-8");
73:   }
74: 
75:   async clearHistory(sessionId: string): Promise<void> {
76:     const chatPath = this.getChatPath(sessionId);
77:     if (existsSync(chatPath)) {
78:       const { unlinkSync } = require("fs");
79:       unlinkSync(chatPath);
80:     }
81:   }
82: }
83: 
84: export const chatService = new ChatService();

### Tool Call [completed]: packages/mimo-platform/src/projects/routes.tsx

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:45:48
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/packages/mimo-platform/src/projects/routes.tsx
oldString: // Delete project (POST /projects/:id/delete)
projects.post("/:id/delete", authMiddleware, async (c) => {
newString: // Freeze project (POST /projects/:id/freeze)
projects.post("/:id/freeze", authMiddleware, async (c) => {
  const id = c.req.param("id");
  const project = await projectRepository.findById(id);
  
  if (!project) {
    return c.notFound();
  }

  const user = c.get("user") as { username: string };
  if (project.owner !== user.username) {
    return c.notFound();
  }

  // Get all sessions for this project and freeze them
  const sessions = await sessionRepository.listByProject(id);
  for (const session of sessions) {
    await sessionRepository.update(session.id, { status: "frozen" });
  }

  return c.redirect(`/projects/${id}`, 302);
});

// Delete project (POST /projects/:id/delete)

294:   
295:   for (const impact of impacts) {
296:     const session = allSessions.find(s => s.id === impact.sessionId);
297:     sessionMap.set(impact.sessionId, {
298:       id: impact.sessionId,
299:       name: impact.sessionName,
300:       exists: !!session,
301:     });
302:   }
303: 
304:   return c.html(
305:     <ImpactHistoryPage 
306:       project={project}
307:       impacts={impacts}
308:       sessions={sessionMap}
309:     />
310:   );
311: });
312: 
313: // Nested session routes
314: projects.route("/:projectId/sessions", sessions);
315: 
316: export default projects;

(End of file - total 316 lines)
</content>
```

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/project-freeze/specs/session-freeze/spec.md

**Tool:** read
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:45:48
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/project-freeze/specs/session-freeze/spec.md

```
<path>/home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/project-freeze/specs/session-freeze/spec.md</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>1: ## ADDED Requirements
2: 
3: ### Requirement: Session status includes frozen state
4: The session status enum SHALL include `frozen` as a valid status value.
5: 
6: #### Scenario: Session created with active status
7: - **WHEN** a new session is created
8: - **THEN** the session status SHALL be set to `active`
9: 
10: #### Scenario: Session status can be set to frozen
11: - **GIVEN** a session with status `active`
12: - **WHEN** the session status is updated to `frozen`
13: - **THEN** the session status SHALL be `frozen`
14: 
15: ### Requirement: Project freeze action marks all sessions as frozen
16: The system SHALL provide a project-level action that marks all sessions belonging to that project as `frozen`.
17: 
18: #### Scenario: Freeze project with multiple sessions
19: - **GIVEN** a project with 3 sessions (all with status `active`)
20: - **WHEN** the "Freeze Project" action is invoked
21: - **THEN** all 3 sessions SHALL have status `frozen`
22: 
23: #### Scenario: Freeze project with no sessions
24: - **GIVEN** a project with 0 sessions
25: - **WHEN** the "Freeze Project" action is invoked
26: - **THEN** no error SHALL occur
27: 
28: #### Scenario: Freeze project with mixed session statuses
29: - **GIVEN** a project with sessions having statuses `active`, `paused`, and `closed`
30: - **WHEN** the "Freeze Project" action is invoked
31: - **THEN** all sessions SHALL have status `frozen`
32: 
33: ### Requirement: Chat messages blocked for frozen sessions
34: The system SHALL reject chat message requests for sessions with status `frozen`.
35: 
36: #### Scenario: Send message to frozen session
37: - **GIVEN** a session with status `frozen`
38: - **WHEN** a chat message is sent to that session
39: - **THEN** the system SHALL return an error indicating the session is frozen
40: - **AND** the message SHALL NOT be processed
41: 
42: #### Scenario: Send message to active session
43: - **GIVEN** a session with status `active`
44: - **WHEN** a chat message is sent to that session
45: - **THEN** the message SHALL be processed normally
46: 
47: ### Requirement: Commits blocked for frozen sessions
48: The system SHALL reject commit requests for sessions with status `frozen`.
49: 
50: #### Scenario: Commit from frozen session
51: - **GIVEN** a session with status `frozen`
52: - **WHEN** a commit is attempted from that session
53: - **THEN** the system SHALL return an error indicating the session is frozen
54: - **AND** the commit SHALL NOT be executed
55: 
56: #### Scenario: Commit from active session
57: - **GIVEN** a session with status `active`
58: - **WHEN** a commit is attempted from that session
59: - **THEN** the commit SHALL be executed normally
60: 
61: ### Requirement: Frozen status displayed in sessions list
62: The system SHALL display the `frozen` status in the sessions list.
63: 
64: #### Scenario: View sessions list with frozen session
65: - **GIVEN** a project with one session having status `frozen`
66: - **WHEN** the sessions list is viewed
67: - **THEN** the session SHALL display status as "frozen"
68: 
69: ### Requirement: Freeze project button in UI
70: The system SHALL provide a "Freeze Project" button on the Project Detail page.
71: 
72: #### Scenario: Project detail page displays freeze button
73: - **GIVEN** a project exists
74: - **WHEN** the Project Detail page is viewed
75: - **THEN** a "Freeze Project" button SHALL be visible in the Actions section
76: 
77: #### Scenario: Click freeze button
78: - **GIVEN** the Project Detail page is displayed
79: - **WHEN** the "Freeze Project" button is clicked
80: - **THEN** all sessions for the project SHALL be marked as `frozen`
81: - **AND** the page SHALL reflect the updated statuses

(End of file - total 81 lines)
</content>
```

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/project-freeze/specs/session-freeze/spec.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:45:48
**Parameters:**
content: ## ADDED Requirements

### Requirement: Session status includes frozen state
The session status enum SHALL include `frozen` as a valid status value.

#### Scenario: Session created with active status
- **WHEN** a new session is created
- **THEN** the session status SHALL be set to `active`

#### Scenario: Session status can be set to frozen
- **GIVEN** a session with status `active`
- **WHEN** the session status is updated to `frozen`
- **THEN** the session status SHALL be `frozen`

### Requirement: Project freeze action marks all sessions as frozen
The system SHALL provide a project-level action that marks all sessions belonging to that project as `frozen`.

#### Scenario: Freeze project with multiple sessions
- **GIVEN** a project with 3 sessions (all with status `active`)
- **WHEN** the "Freeze Project" action is invoked
- **THEN** all 3 sessions SHALL have status `frozen`

#### Scenario: Freeze project with no sessions
- **GIVEN** a project with 0 sessions
- **WHEN** the "Freeze Project" action is invoked
- **THEN** no error SHALL occur

#### Scenario: Freeze project with mixed session statuses
- **GIVEN** a project with sessions having statuses `active`, `paused`, and `closed`
- **WHEN** the "Freeze Project" action is invoked
- **THEN** all sessions SHALL have status `frozen`

### Requirement: Chat messages blocked for frozen sessions
The system SHALL reject chat message requests for sessions with status `frozen`.

#### Scenario: Send message to frozen session
- **GIVEN** a session with status `frozen`
- **WHEN** a chat message is sent to that session
- **THEN** the system SHALL return an error indicating the session is frozen
- **AND** the message SHALL NOT be processed

#### Scenario: Send message to active session
- **GIVEN** a session with status `active`
- **WHEN** a chat message is sent to that session
- **THEN** the message SHALL be processed normally

### Requirement: Commits blocked for frozen sessions
The system SHALL reject commit requests for sessions with status `frozen`.

#### Scenario: Commit from frozen session
- **GIVEN** a session with status `frozen`
- **WHEN** a commit is attempted from that session
- **THEN** the system SHALL return an error indicating the session is frozen
- **AND** the commit SHALL NOT be executed

#### Scenario: Commit from active session
- **GIVEN** a session with status `active`
- **WHEN** a commit is attempted from that session
- **THEN** the commit SHALL be executed normally

### Requirement: Frozen status displayed in sessions list
The system SHALL display the `frozen` status in the sessions list.

#### Scenario: View sessions list with frozen session
- **GIVEN** a project with one session having status `frozen`
- **WHEN** the sessions list is viewed
- **THEN** the session SHALL display status as "frozen"

### Requirement: Freeze project button in UI
The system SHALL provide a "Freeze Project" button on the Project Detail page.

#### Scenario: Project detail page displays freeze button
- **GIVEN** a project exists
- **WHEN** the Project Detail page is viewed
- **THEN** a "Freeze Project" button SHALL be visible in the Actions section

#### Scenario: Click freeze button
- **GIVEN** the Project Detail page is displayed
- **WHEN** the "Freeze Project" button is clicked
- **THEN** all sessions for the project SHALL be marked as `frozen`
- **AND** the page SHALL reflect the updated statuses

filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/project-freeze/specs/session-freeze/spec.md

```

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/project-freeze/design.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:45:48
**Parameters:**
content: ## Context

The MIMO platform uses sessions to isolate work on projects. Each session has a `status` field currently supporting `active`, `paused`, and `closed`. When external changes occur in the upstream repository, users need a way to freeze all sessions to prevent editing stale state.

The freeze operation is a project-level action that affects all sessions belonging to that project. Once frozen, sessions remain viewable but cannot accept new edits or commits.

## Goals / Non-Goals

**Goals:**
- Provide a one-click "Freeze Project" action that marks all sessions as `frozen`
- Prevent chat message sending on frozen sessions
- Prevent commit operations on frozen sessions
- Display `frozen` status clearly in the sessions list

**Non-Goals:**
- Automatic freeze detection (this is manual user action)
- Unfreezing sessions (create new sessions instead)
- Visual badges or icons (just status text)
- Changes to agent-workspace file system
- Interruption of running agents

## Decisions

**1. New `frozen` status value**
- Extends existing status enum: `"active" | "paused" | "closed" | "frozen"`
- Frozen sessions are distinct from paused (paused can be resumed, frozen cannot)
- Simple enum addition avoids complex state machines

**2. Project-level freeze action**
- POST endpoint: `/projects/:id/freeze`
- Iterates all sessions for the project and updates status to `frozen`
- No atomic transaction needed (eventual consistency is acceptable)

**3. Minimal UI changes**
- Single "Freeze Project" button in Project Detail Actions section
- Status displays as plain text "frozen" in sessions list
- No special styling or badges requested

**4. Blocking at API level**
- Check `session.status === 'frozen'` before processing chat messages
- Check `session.status === 'frozen'` before processing commits
- Return appropriate error message indicating session is frozen

## Risks / Trade-offs

- **Risk**: Users may accidentally freeze projects
  - Mitigation: Add confirmation dialog (optional, can be skipped per user preference)
  
- **Risk**: Frozen sessions accumulate over time
  - Mitigation: Archive functionality already exists for cleanup

- **Trade-off**: No unfreeze operation means users must create new sessions
  - Rationale: Keeps implementation simple, frozen sessions serve as historical record

filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/project-freeze/design.md

```
Wrote file successfully.

│ changes │
╰─────────╯

+## Context
+
+The MIMO platform uses sessions to isolate work on projects. Each session has a `status` field currently supporting `active`, `paused`, and `closed`. When external changes occur in the upstream repository, users need a way to freeze all sessions to prevent editing stale state.
+
+The freeze operation is a project-level action that affects all sessions belonging to that project. Once frozen, sessions remain viewable but cannot accept new edits or commits.
+
+## Goals / Non-Goals
+
+**Goals:**
+- Provide a one-click "Freeze Project" action that marks all sessions as `frozen`
+- Prevent chat message sending on frozen sessions
+- Prevent commit operations on frozen sessions
+- Display `frozen` status clearly in the sessions list
+
+**Non-Goals:**
+- Automatic freeze detection (this is manual user action)
+- Unfreezing sessions (create new sessions instead)
+- Visual badges or icons (just status text)
+- Changes to agent-workspace file system
+- Interruption of running agents
+
+## Decisions
+
+**1. New `frozen` status value**
+- Extends existing status enum: `"active" | "paused" | "closed" | "frozen"`
+- Frozen sessions are distinct from paused (paused can be resumed, frozen cannot)
+- Simple enum addition avoids complex state machines
+
+**2. Project-level freeze action**
+- POST endpoint: `/projects/:id/freeze`
+- Iterates all sessions for the project and updates status to `frozen`
+- No atomic transaction needed (eventual consistency is acceptable)
+
+**3. Minimal UI changes**
+- Single "Freeze Project" button in Project Detail Actions section
+- Status displays as plain text "frozen" in sessions list
+- No special styling or badges requested
+
+**4. Blocking at API level**
+- Check `session.status === 'frozen'` before processing chat messages
+- Check `session.status === 'frozen'` before processing commits
+- Return appropriate error message indicating session is frozen
+
+## Risks / Trade-offs
+
+- **Risk**: Users may accidentally freeze projects
+  - Mitigation: Add confirmation dialog (optional, can be skipped per user preference)
+  
+- **Risk**: Frozen sessions accumulate over time
+  - Mitigation: Archive functionality already exists for cleanup
+
+- **Trade-off**: No unfreeze operation means users must create new sessions
+  - Rationale: Keeps implementation simple, frozen sessions serve as historical record

3: When external changes are pushed to a project's upstream repository, existing sessions become stale. Users need a way to mark all sessions as frozen to prevent accidental edits on outdated state. Currently, there's no mechanism to lock sessions when the external repository has moved forward.
4: 
5: ## What Changes
6:

11: - Block commit operations for frozen sessions
12: - Display `frozen` status in sessions list (no badge/icon, just text)
13:

15: 
16: ### New Capabilities
17: - `session-freeze`: Session status management with frozen state and project-level freeze action
18: 
19: ### Modified Capabilities
20: - None (existing session behavior remains unchanged, just adding new status value)
21: 
22: ## Impact
23: 
24: - Session repository: new `frozen` status value
25: - Project Detail UI: new button and action
26: - Session routes: validation to block messages/commits for frozen sessions
27: - Session list UI: display frozen status

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/project-freeze/proposal.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-08 22:45:48
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/project-freeze/proposal.md
content: ## Why

When external changes are pushed to a project's upstream repository, existing sessions become stale. Users need a way to mark all sessions as frozen to prevent accidental edits on outdated state. Currently, there's no mechanism to lock sessions when the external repository has moved forward.

## What Changes

- Add `frozen` status to session status enum (`active | paused | closed` → `active | paused | closed | frozen`)
- Create new project action "Freeze Project" that marks all sessions as `frozen`
- Add "Freeze Project" button to Project Detail page (Actions section, next to Delete)
- Block chat message sending for frozen sessions
- Block commit operations for frozen sessions
- Display `frozen` status in sessions list (no badge/icon, just text)

## Capabilities

### New Capabilities
- `session-freeze`: Session status management with frozen state and project-level freeze action

### Modified Capabilities
- None (existing session behavior remains unchanged, just adding new status value)

## Impact

- Session repository: new `frozen` status value
- Project Detail UI: new button and action
- Session routes: validation to block messages/commits for frozen sessions
- Session list UI: display frozen status


```

╰─────────╯

@@ -0,0 +1,27 @@
+## Why
+
+When external changes are pushed to a project's upstream repository, existing sessions become stale. Users need a way to mark all sessions as frozen to prevent accidental edits on outdated state. Currently, there's no mechanism to lock sessions when the external repository has moved forward.
+
+## What Changes
+
+- Add `frozen` status to session status enum (`active | paused | closed` → `active | paused | closed | frozen`)
+- Create new project action "Freeze Project" that marks all sessions as `frozen`
+- Add "Freeze Project" button to Project Detail page (Actions section, next to Delete)
+- Block chat message sending for frozen sessions
+- Block commit operations for frozen sessions
+- Display `frozen` status in sessions list (no badge/icon, just text)
+
+## Capabilities
+
+### New Capabilities
+- `session-freeze`: Session status management with frozen state and project-level freeze action
+
+### Modified Capabilities
+- None (existing session behavior remains unchanged, just adding new status value)
+
+## Impact
+
+- Session repository: new `frozen` status value
+- Project Detail UI: new button and action
+- Session routes: validation to block messages/commits for frozen sessions
+- Session list UI: display frozen status
```

62:

64:     return join(this.getProjectPath(id), "project.yaml");

66:

68:     return crypto.randomUUID();
69:   }

71:   async create(input: CreateProjectInput): Promise<Project> {
72:     if (input.description && input.description.length > 500) {
73:       throw new Error("Description must be 500 characters or less");
74:     }
75: 
76:     const id = this.generateId();
77:     const projectPath = this.getProjectPath(id);
78:     
79:     if (!existsSync(projectPath)) {
80:       mkdirSync(projectPath, { recursive: true });
81:     }
82: 
83:     const projectData: ProjectData = {
84:       id,
85:       name: input.name,
86:       repoUrl: input.repoUrl,
87:       repoType: input.repoType,
88:       owner: input.owner,
89:       createdAt: new Date().toISOString(),

91:       ...(input.credentialId && { credentialId: input.credentialId }),
92:       ...(input.sourceBranch && { sourceBranch: input.sourceBranch }),

95:     };
96:

98:       this.getProjectFilePath(id),
99:       dump(projectData),
100:       "utf-8"
101:     );
102: 
103:     return {
104:       ...projectData,
105:       createdAt: new Date(projectData.createdAt),
106:     };
107:   }

109:   async findById(id: string): Promise<Project | null> {
110:     const filePath = this.getProjectFilePath(id);
111:     if (!existsSync(filePath)) {
112:       return null;
113:     }
114: 
115:     const content = readFileSync(filePath, "utf-8");
116:     const data = load(content) as ProjectData;
117:     
118:     return {
119:       ...data,
120:       createdAt: new Date(data.createdAt),
121:     };
122:   }
123: 
124:   async listByOwner(owner: string): Promise<Project[]> {
125:     const Paths = getPaths();
126:     if (!existsSync(Paths.projects)) {
127:       return [];
128:     }
129: 
130:     const entries = readdirSync(Paths.projects, { withFileTypes: true });
131:     const projects: Project[] = [];
132: 
133:     for (const entry of entries) {
134:       if (entry.isDirectory()) {
135:         const projectFile = join(Paths.projects, entry.name, "project.yaml");
136:         if (existsSync(projectFile)) {
137:           const content = readFileSync(projectFile, "utf-8");
138:           const data = load(content) as ProjectData;
139:           if (data.owner === owner) {
140:             projects.push({
141:               ...data,
142:               createdAt: new Date(data.createdAt),
143:             });
144:           }
145:         }
146:       }
147:     }
148: 
149:     return projects;
150:   }

178:   async listAllPublic(): Promise<PublicProject[]> {
179:     const projects = await this.listAll();
180:     return projects.map(project => ({
181:       id: project.id,
182:       name: project.name,
183:       description: project.description,
184:       repoType: project.repoType,
185:       owner: project.owner,
186:       createdAt: project.createdAt.toISOString(),
187:     }));
188:   }
189: 
190:   async delete(id: string): Promise<void> {
191:     const projectPath = this.getProjectPath(id);
192:     
193:     if (existsSync(projectPath)) {
194:       // Delete project.yaml first
195:       const projectFile = this.getProjectFilePath(id);
196:       if (existsSync(projectFile)) {
197:         unlinkSync(projectFile);
198:       }
199:       
200:       // Delete any other files in the directory
201:       const entries = readdirSync(projectPath);
202:       for (const entry of entries) {
203:         const entryPath = join(projectPath, entry);
204:         if (existsSync(entryPath)) {
205:           unlinkSync(entryPath);
206:         }
207:       }
208:       
209:       // Delete the directory
210:       rmdirSync(projectPath);
211:     }
212:   }
213: 
214:   async exists(id: string): Promise<boolean> {
215:     return existsSync(this.getProjectFilePath(id));
216:   }
217: 
218:   async update(id: string, updates: { name?: string; repoUrl?: string; repoType?: "git" | "fossil"; description?: string; credentialId?: string; defaultLocalDevMirrorPath?: string | null }): Promise<Project> {
219:     const project = await this.findById(id);
220:     if (!project) {
221:       throw new Error("Project not found");
222:     }
223: 
224:     if (updates.description && updates.description.length > 500) {
225:       throw new Error("Description must be 500 characters or less");
226:     }
227: 
228:     const updatedData: ProjectData = {
229:       id: project.id,
230:       name: updates.name || project.name,
231:       repoUrl: updates.repoUrl || project.repoUrl,
232:       repoType: updates.repoType || project.repoType,
233:       owner: project.owner,
234:       createdAt: project.createdAt.toISOString(),
235:       description: updates.description,
236:       sourceBranch: project.sourceBranch,
237:       newBranch: project.newBranch,
238:       defaultLocalDevMirrorPath: updates.defaultLocalDevMirrorPath !== undefined ? updates.defaultLocalDevMirrorPath : project.defaultLocalDevMirrorPath,
239:     };
240: 
241:     // Handle credentialId specially - if undefined, keep existing; if null, remove; if string, set
242:     if ("credentialId" in updates) {
243:       if (updates.credentialId !== undefined) {
244:         updatedData.credentialId = updates.credentialId;
245:       }
246:     } else if (project.credentialId) {
247:       updatedData.credentialId = project.credentialId;
248:     }
249: 
250:     writeFileSync(
251:       this.getProjectFilePath(id),
252:       dump(updatedData),
253:       "utf-8"
254:     );
255: 
256:     return {
257:       ...updatedData,

259:     };

201:     if (assignedAgentId && agentService.isAgentOnline(assignedAgentId)) {
202:       const agentWs = agentService.getAgentConnection(assignedAgentId);
203:       if (agentWs && agentWs.readyState === 1) {
204:         const serverResult = await fossilServerManager.startServer(session.id, fossilPath);
205:         if ('port' in serverResult) {

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-08 22:49:27)

Ah! Now I see it clearly. Looking at the session creation code:

1. **Project creation** (`projects/repository.ts` line 71-107): Only creates a project.yaml file - NO repository is cloned at project creation time.

2. **Session creation** (`sessions/routes.tsx` line 136-148): When a session is created, it CLONES the repository from the remote URL directly into `session.upstreamPath`.

So the flow is:
1. User creates project → only creates project.yaml (no repo)
2. User creates session → clones remote repo directly to session's `upstream/`

This means:
- **Project doesn't have an `original/` repository** - it's just metadata
- **Each session has its own `upstream/` clone** from when it was created
- The session's `upstream/` is a snapshot of the remote at session creation time

So when user says "pull remote changes to upstream", they mean:
- Pull from remote repository → session's `upstream/` directory

And since each session has its own independent clone, when you "Sync" (pull remote), you need to:
1. For each session, pull latest from remote to that session's `upstream/`
2. Freeze the session

This is different from what was built! The current implementation just freezes sessions without pulling anything.

Now I understand the confusion. The user wants to:
1. Pull remote changes to each session's `upstream/` 
2. Then freeze the session

NOT just freeze sessions without pulling.
## Agent (2026-04-08 22:49:32)

Now I see it clearly. Let me trace the actual flow:

```
PROJECT vs SESSION CREATION
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

Create Project
     │
     ▼
┌────────────┐
│ project.yaml│  ← Just metadata, NO repo here
│ (no repo)  │
└────────────┘
     │
     │ Create Session
     ▼
┌────────────┐         ┌──────────────────┐
│ Session    │◄────────│ Clone from       │
│ upstream/  │         │ remote URL       │
│ (has repo) │         │ to upstream/     │
└────────────┘         └──────────────────┘

```

So **projects don't have a repository** - only sessions do! Each session clones directly from remote at creation time.

This means when you say "pull remote changes to upstream", you mean:
- Pull from remote → each session's `upstream/` directory

**Current "Freeze" implementation:**
- ❌ Just marks sessions frozen (no pull)

**What you actually want:**
- Pull remote → each session's `upstream/` 
- Then freeze sessions

Is that right? The "Sync" button should:
1. For each session: `git pull` (or fossil sync) in their `upstream/`
2. Then freeze all sessions

Correct?
